# /isorender - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#isorender)

/isorender[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#isorender "Permanent link")

===============================================================================================================

The `/isorender` command sits at the very core of Isometric Renders. It is your primary interface for launching all rendering operations and is also used to enter [Unsafe Mode](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/home/#unsafe-mode)
.

* * *

Single Render Operations[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#single-render-operations "Permanent link")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### `/isorender item`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#isorender-item "Permanent link")

Render the given item, including NBT. If the item is omitted, render the player's current item instead

Examples

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-0-1) # render your current item [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-0-2) /isorender item  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-0-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-0-4) # render a diamond [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-0-5) /isorender item minecraft:diamond  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-0-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-0-7) # render an enchanted diamond sword [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-0-8) /isorender item minecraft:diamond_sword{Enchantments:[{id:"sharpness",lvl:10}]}`

### `/isorender block`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#isorender-block "Permanent link")

Render the given block, including NBT and block state data. If the block is omitted, render whichever block the player is currently looking at

The water in waterlogged block will not be visible in a block render. If you do want a render of that, simply do a single-block area render (as explained below) instead

Examples

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-1-1) # render the block you're looking at [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-1-2) /isorender block [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-1-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-1-4) # render cobblestone [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-1-5) /isorender block minecraft:cobblestone [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-1-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-1-7) # render a burning furnace with coal inside it [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-1-8) /isorender block minecraft:furnace[lit=true]{Items:[{Slot:0b, Count: 1b, id: "minecraft:coal"}]}`

### `/isorender entity`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#isorender-entity "Permanent link")

Render the given entity, including NBT as an optional second argument. If the entity is omitted, render whichever entity the player is currently looking at

Examples

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-2-1) # render the entity you're looking at [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-2-2) /isorender entity [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-2-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-2-4) # render a blaze [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-2-5) /isorender entity minecraft:blaze [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-2-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-2-7) # render a baby zombie [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-2-8) /isorender entity minecraft:zombie {IsBaby:1b}`

### `/isorender area`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#isorender-area "Permanent link")

Render the area of the world between the two given block coordinate triples. If coordinates are omitted, render the current [Area Selection](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/home/#visual-area-selection)
 instead.

Examples

`` [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-3-1) # render the current area selection [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-3-2) /isorender area [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-3-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-3-4) # render the area between the given coodinate triples [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-3-5) /isorender area 3 63 -120 8 66 -123` ``

### `/isorender tooltip`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#isorender-tooltip "Permanent link")

Render the given item's tooltip, including NBT. If the item is omitted, render the tooltip of the player's current item instead

Examples

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-4-1) # render the tooltip of your current item [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-4-2) /isorender tooltip  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-4-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-4-4) # render the tooltip of a netherite pickaxe enchanted with efficiency 5 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-4-5) /isorender tooltip minecraft:netherite_pickaxe{Enchantments:[{id:"efficiency",lvl:5}]}`

Batch Render Operations[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#batch-render-operations "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

All batch render commands first select some set of items and end with a **render task argument**. This can be one of three things:

*   `atlas`, which renders an atlas (or overview if you will) of the item set
*   `batch items`, which renders each item in the set individually
*   `batch blocks`, which renders the corresponding block of each item in the set individually

### `/isorender creative_tab`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#isorender-creative_tab "Permanent link")

Select all items from the given creative inventory tab

Examples

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-5-1) # render an atlas of all items in the brewing creative tab [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-5-2) /isorender creative_tab brewing atlas [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-5-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-5-4) # render each block in the redstone creative tab individually [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-5-5) /isorender creative_tab redstone batch blocks`

### `/isorender tag`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#isorender-tag "Permanent link")

Select all items from the given item tag

Examples

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-6-1) # render an atlas of all iron ores [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-6-2) /isorender tag #minecraft:iron_ores atlas [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-6-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-6-4) # render each anvil state individually [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-6-5) /isorender tag #minecraft:anvil batch blocks`

### `/isorender namespace`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#isorender-namespace "Permanent link")

Select all items from the given namespace

Examples

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-7-1) # render an atlas of every single item in minecraft [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-7-2) /isorender namespace minecraft atlas [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-7-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-7-4) # render each block in minecraft individually [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/isometric-renders/slash_isorender/#__codelineno-7-5) /isorender namespace minecraft batch blocks`

* * *

# Limelight - Wisp Forest Docs

 

Limelight
=========

Welcome to Limelight's documentation! Limelight is an extensible command palette for Minecraft, meant to allow users to easily search for and run actions.

If you want to write a resource pack, take a look at the **Configuring** section.  
If you want to make a Limelight addon or add compatibility, go to the [Extending](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/)
 section.

* * *

Last update: 1 year ago2024-08-30

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/#)

# FAQ - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/faq/#faq)

FAQ[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/faq/#faq "Permanent link")

====================================================================

I get disconnected due to an "\[oωo\] handshake failure" when trying to join a server[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/faq/#i-get-disconnected-due-to-an-oo-handshake-failure-when-trying-to-join-a-server "Permanent link")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   **The server is running a proxy:** If the server is using a proxy which is not Velocity, there is nothing you can do. If the server is running Velocity, install the [oωo velocity plugin](https://modrinth.com/plugin/owo-velocity-plugin)
     on the proxy.
    
*   **The server is not using a proxy:** This means that the installed mods on the server and your game are not matching up. Try making sure that all the mod versions are the same and they are being properly loaded
    

If neither of these approaches fix your problem, [open an issue](https://github.com/wisp-forest/owo-lib/issues/new/choose)

* * *

My game crashes due to a `Non [a-z0-9/._-] character in path of location`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/faq/#my-game-crashes-due-to-a-non-a-z0-9_-character-in-path-of-location "Permanent link")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Upgrade oωo to any version newer than 0.6.0+1.18

* * *

My Conjurer does not spawn anything[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/faq/#my-conjurer-does-not-spawn-anything "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Conjuring

Check that the spawn conditions are right - for example most animals require grass, most monsters require darkness and so on. If you're sure these are correct, verify that mobs are even allowed to spawn in the first place - the _Big Torch_ from _Kibe_ is a common problem, as it blocks the Conjurer and all other spawners in addition to natural mob spawning.

* * *

Why can the Shop not buy Items[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/faq/#why-can-the-shop-not-buy-items "Permanent link")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Numismatic Overhaul

The Shop cannot buy items for a single reason - it would almost certainly not be very useful because it's highly impractical. Imagine this: You, the buyer, need some amount of a specific item. Thus, you put a shop which buys that item for some amount of money. You now have to wait for someone to randomly discover that you want this item and you need that someone to actually have said item on hand. This means your deals will very rarely actually go through. Instead, you could've just asked in chat or through some other means and gotten your items faster and more conveniently by simply trading in person.

* * *

How do I reset my area selection[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/faq/#how-do-i-reset-my-area-selection "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Isometric Renders

Sneak while pressing the select hotkey

* * *

I can't see Chests/Shulker Boxes/Bells/... in my area renders[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/faq/#i-cant-see-chestsshulker-boxesbells-in-my-area-renders "Permanent link")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Isometric Renders

Upgrade Isometric Renders to any version newer than [0.3.0](https://modrinth.com/mod/isometric-renders/version/0.3.0%2B1.19)

* * *

Last update: 3 years ago2023-01-04

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/faq/#)

# Villager Trade Data Format - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#villager-trade-data-format)

Villager Trade Data Format[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#villager-trade-data-format "Permanent link")

=========================================================================================================================================

All trade definition files belong in `data/numismatic-overhaul/villager_trades`. You can define as many files for a villager profession as you like, although having multiple files per profession is discouraged for the sake of simplicity.

All the trades are collected based on profession, and for each level the villager randomly picks their trades.

**Wandering Trader**

The Wandering Trader is a special case. Its profession ID is `wandering_trader`, and it only requires trades for the `novice` and `apprentice` levels. Any other trades will not load.

* * *

File Format[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#file-format "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Each trade definition file needs two elements in the root object:

*   `profession`: The profession the following trades are for, without namespace (eg. `"profession": "farmer"`)
    
*   `trades`: The trades for this profession, one array for each level
    

**Example:**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-2)   "profession": "farmer", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-3)   "trades": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-4)     "novice": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-5)       { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-6)         "type": ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-7)         ...options... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-8)       }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-9)       { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-10)         "type": ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-11)         ...options... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-12)       } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-13)     ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-14)   } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-0-15) }`

### ItemStack format[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#itemstack-format "Permanent link")

| Property | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `id` | The item ID | string |
| `count` | The item count | int _optional_ |
| `tag` | An NBT tag | A nested object _optional_ |

Example

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-1-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-1-2)   "id": "minecraft:diamond_pickaxe", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-1-3)   "count": 1 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-1-4)   "tag": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-1-5)     "Damage": 75 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-1-6)   } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-1-7) }`

Trade Types[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#trade-types "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**All trades types** have these optional parameters:

| Parameter | Description | Type | Default |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `price_multiplier` | The multiplier to apply when a player has gossip | float | 0.05 |
| `max_uses` | The max uses of this trade before restocking | int | 12  |
| `villager_experience` | The experience awarded to the villager when using this trade | int | 5   |

* * *

### Buy Item[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#buy-item "Permanent link")

`numismatic-overhaul:buy_stack`

The Villager **buys** the given stack for the given price

| Parameter | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `price` | Price in bronze coins | int |
| `buy` | The item to buy | ItemStack |

Example

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-2-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-2-2)   "type": "numismatic-overhaul:buy_item", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-2-3)   "buy": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-2-4)     "item": "minecraft:brown_wool", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-2-5)     "count": 6 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-2-6)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-2-7)   "price": 74000 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-2-8) }`

* * *

### Sell Item[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#sell-item "Permanent link")

`numismatic-overhaul:sell_stack`

The Villager **sells** the given stack for the given price

| Parameter | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `price` | Price in bronze coins | int |
| `sell` | The item to sell | ItemStack |

Example

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-3-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-3-2)   "type": "numismatic-overhaul:sell_stack", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-3-3)   "sell": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-3-4)     "item": "minecraft:cookie", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-3-5)     "count": 2 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-3-6)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-3-7)   "price": 65, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-3-8)   "max_uses": 2 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-3-9) }`

* * *

### Process Item[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#process-item "Permanent link")

`numismatic-overhaul:process_item`

Sells an item for another item and some money

| Parameter | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `sell` | The item to sell | ItemStack |
| `buy` | The item to process | ItemStack |
| `price` | The price in bronze coins | int |

Example

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-4-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-4-2)   "type": "numismatic-overhaul:process_item", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-4-3)   "sell": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-4-4)     "item": "minecraft:diamond" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-4-5)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-4-6)   "buy": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-4-7)     "item": "minecraft:emerald" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-4-8)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-4-9)   "price": 2000 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-4-10) }`

* * *

### Sell Map[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#sell-map "Permanent link")

`numismatic-overhaul:sell_map`

Sells a map for a specific structure

| Parameter | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `price` | The price in bronze coins | int |
| `structure` | The structure id, you can find these out using `/locate` | string |

Example

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-5-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-5-2)   "type": "numismatic-overhaul:sell_map", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-5-3)   "structure": "minecraft:endcity", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-5-4)   "price": 5, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-5-5)   "villager_experience": 20 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-5-6) }`

* * *

### Sell Item in Dimension[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#sell-item-in-dimension "Permanent link")

`numismatic-overhaul:dimension_sell_stack`

Sells the given stack for the given price, but only if the villager is in the given dimension

| Parameter | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `price` | The price in bronze coins | int |
| `sell` | The item to sell | ItemStack |
| `dimension` | The dimension to sell in | string |

Example

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-6-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-6-2)   "type": "numismatic-overhaul:dimension_sell_stack", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-6-3)   "sell": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-6-4)     "item": "minecraft:cookie", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-6-5)     "count": 2 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-6-6)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-6-7)   "price": 65, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-6-8)   "max_uses": 2, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-6-9)   "dimension": "minecraft:the_end" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-6-10) }`

* * *

Sells a single random enchantment, prices are calculated based on the generated enchantments

| `price_multiplier` | Multiplier for the price | int _optional_ |

### Sell Enchanted Item[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#sell-enchanted-item "Permanent link")

Sells an item enchanted at the given level, prices are calculated based on the generated enchantments

| Parameter | Description | Type | Default |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `level` | The level to enchant with, may exceed 30 | int |     |
| `base_price` | A base price in bronze coins on which to base calculations | int _optional_ | 200 |
| `allow_treasure` | Whether to allow treasure enchantments | boolean _optional_ | false |
| `item` | The item to enchant | ItemStack _optional_ | `minecraft:book` |

Example

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-8-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-8-2)   "type": "numismatic-overhaul:enchant_item", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-8-3)   "base_price": 250, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-8-4)   "level": 30, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-8-5)   "allow_treasure": true, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-8-6)   "item": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-8-7)     "item": "minecraft:diamond_sword" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-8-8)   } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/numismatic-overhaul/trades/#__codelineno-8-9) }`

# Features - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#registration)

Features
========

### [Registration](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/)
[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#registration "Permanent link")

0.1.3

oωo offers a flexible system for automatically registering a class' fields into `Registry` instances. It is very quick to implement and usually eliminates a lot of boilerplate. At the same time though, it is extremely flexible and allows significant customization and complete control over how the fields are processed using the `FieldProcessingSuject` API tree.

### Networking[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#networking "Permanent link")

0.4.0

oωo provides a fully-featured network serialization system. Built around `OwoNetChannel` and the `PacketBufSerializer` framework, packet data is automatically (de-)serialized and the corresponding handlers invoked without the need of keeping track of Identifiers or channel associations - everything is derived from the data class. Packet contents are defined as Java `record`s, making it highly ergonomic. The serialization backend fully supports serializers for custom types and all channel-layout related data is synced between client and server making it so an incompatible server cannot be joined.

### [Item Groups](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/)
[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#item-groups "Permanent link")

0.2.0

The Item Group API allows you to create an Item Group with custom textures and sub-tabs in very few lines of code. It is still pretty open to customization and can make custom buttons for linking to your mod's project pages or even executing custom actions relevant to your mod.

### Particle Effects[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#particle-effects "Permanent link")

0.1.0

oωo provides two main systems for handling particles. Primarily there's a client-sided set of utility methods for displaying multiple particles in the world, including drawing lines and cubes, randomized velocity and other general utility. To then allow easily composing and triggering these methods from the server, the `ParticleSystem` API, built on top of oωo's networking stack, can be used.

### Debug/Dev Features[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#debugdev-features "Permanent link")

0.3.0

When in a development environment, oωo's debug mode is automatically enabled which adds a host of features like commands for damaging/healing the player or dumping information about game objects, automatically disabled weather and daylight cycle and a few more.

### Moddata[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#moddata "Permanent link")

0.3.0

The `ModDataLoader` and related API are designed to allow loading JSON-formatted data from the `mod` directory of all present mods. This makes it very easy to utilize datapack-like files for data that needs to be available before a world is loaded. For the purposes of modpack customization, the files are loaded from `.minecraft/moddata` as a replacement for datapacks.

### Screen Utilities[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#screen-utilities "Permanent link")

0.3.0

oωo contains a few very simple helpers to facilitate the creation of a simple `HandledScreen` and `ScreenHandler`, namely a type of slot that only allows certain items as well as methods for generating the player inventory slots required for almost all screens.

### NBT Handling[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#nbt-handling "Permanent link")

0.7.0

The `NbtKey` class is a simple serialization wrapper that allows inserting and extracting data values from `NbtCompound` instances. It essentially wraps the `get(...)` and `put(...)` methods to eliminate magic strings and centralize serialization code.

### Tag Injection[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#tag-injection "Permanent link")

0.3.6

The `TagInjector` system allows you to inject entries into tags at runtime. There are numerous helper methods available for easily injecting blocks and items, but the barebones inject instructions are exposed as well to enable injection into Tags of arbitrary registries.

### Offline Data Access[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#offline-data-access "Permanent link")

0.5.0

The `OfflineDataLookup` and `OfflineAdvancementLookup` interfaces enable easily querying and/or modifying the NBT and Advancement data of offline players. As everything in oωo, the API surface is non-verbose to use and usually does not require more than a single method call.

* * *

Last update: 3 years ago2022-10-04

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/features/#)

---

# Item Groups - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#adding-tabs)

Item Groups
===========

This guide is only applicable for Minecraft versions 1.19.3 and onwards. There were significant changes to the item group system which mandated changes in owo's approach to stay compatible.

Creating a basic owo item group is easy - begin by calling `OwoItemGroup.builder(...)` and supply it with:

*   The identifier to register your group with
*   A function that creates the icon of your group - this is called at a later stage during the initialization process and should use one of the `Icon.of(...)` overloads

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#__codelineno-0-1) public static final OwoItemGroup GROUP = OwoItemGroup [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#__codelineno-0-2)     .builder(new Identifier("mod-id", "item_group"), () -> Icon.of(Mod.ITEM)) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#__codelineno-0-3)     // additional builder configuration goes between these lines [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#__codelineno-0-4)     .build();`

### Adding tabs[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#adding-tabs "Permanent link")

In order to add a tab to your item group, extend your group builder configuration with the `intializer(...)` method. Inside it, call `group.addTab(...)` - this accepts four parameters:

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `icon` | The icon of this tab. Look at the different methods available on the `Icon` class, as this supports more than just items |
| `name` | The name of this tab, used for the translation key |
| `contentTag` ⠀ | The item tag used for populating the content of this tab. If you wish to populate your tabs in code using `OwoItemSettings.tab(...)`, this may be `null` |
| `primary` | If this is `true`, the tab's name is displayed as-is, otherwise the name of the item group itself gets prepended |

About custom tabs

If you want or need more precise control over how the tab is populated, you can use the `group.addCustomTab(...)` function instead. Instead of a tag, it takes a `ContentSupplier` function that is called and provided the `ItemGroup.Entries` to append to when the creative inventory is initialized

### Adding buttons[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#adding-buttons "Permanent link")

Buttons work in much the same way as tabs, except that they usually require fewer parameters. Given that most of the time you would want to link to some external resource, `ItemGroupButton.link(...)` and the related methods like `ItemGroupButton.modrinth(...)` should be of interest. You can then pass this button directly into the `group.addButton(...)` method.

If you want your button to execute a custom action, simply call the constructor directly. It accepts the following parameters:

| Parameter | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `group` | The item group the button belongs to, usually just `group` |
| `icon` | The icon of this button, this works identically as it does for tabs |
| `name` | The name of this button, used for the translation key |
| `action` | The action to run when this button is pressed |

### Configuring the Item Group further[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#configuring-the-item-group-further "Permanent link")

#### Using a custom texture[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#using-a-custom-texture "Permanent link")

In order to change the texture used to render your item group, insert `customTexture(...)` with the ID of the texture you want to use. This texture needs to follow a specific format in order to look correct, for this you can use the [template included in the testmod](https://github.com/wisp-forest/owo-lib/blob/1.19.3/src/testmod/resources/assets/uwu/textures/gui/group.png)
.

#### Configuring stacking height[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#configuring-stacking-height "Permanent link")

The buttons to either side of your item group (that is, tabs on the left and buttons on the right), usually arrange themselves to stack up to a height of 4. Depending on how many tabs or buttons you have, it may make sense to change this. To do so, insert either `tabStackHeight(...)` or `buttonStackHeight(...)`.

#### Making the title static[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#making-the-title-static "Permanent link")

You can insert `disableDynamicTitle()` to force the title of your item group to be static, instead of changing with the tab that is selected.

### Initializing the group[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#initializing-the-group "Permanent link")

After all your items have been registered, it is very important that you call the `initialize()` method on your item group. This will run setup and create the group icon, both of which can cause trouble if executed earlier.

### Using custom stack generators[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#using-custom-stack-generators "Permanent link")

When using `OwoItemSettings` instead of the vanilla `Item.Settings` to configure your item's tabs, you may have noticed the `stackGenerator(...)` setter. Using this, you can change the function which appends your item to the item group. The default function will just call `getDefaultStack()` on your item, which may not always be sufficient. Particularly if you want variations of your item with different NBT data, changing this may prove useful

* * *

Last update: 3 years ago2023-01-29

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/item-groups/#)

---

# Networking - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#concepts)

Networking
==========

~0.4.0~ 0.7.0

Networking can be quite the hassle to set up and maintain when using only the tools provided to you by Minecraft and Fabric API. owo, however, includes an easy-to-use networking stack which is quick to set up and even easier to maintain while still keeping high performance.

Concepts[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#concepts "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

owo's networking API comprises of two core systems - the `OwoNetChannel`, which handles all networking, and the mostly self-contained `PacketBufSerializer`, which takes care of serializing objects into packet buffers.

For safety reasons, using a channel in your mod will enable owo's handshaking procedure. This verifies that the channel layout on both server and client is identical, to prevent possible crashes or malformed data received, if one side is encoding differently than the other expects.

Implementation[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#implementation "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Creating your channel[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#creating-your-channel "Permanent link")

To get started creating your first channel, simply create a new instance of `OwoNetChannel` and store it in a constant field somewhere:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-0-1) ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-0-2) // as long as you use your mod's id here, the path doesn't actually [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-0-3) // matter - it really could be anything [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-0-4) public static final OwoNetChannel MY_CHANNEL = OwoNetChannel.create(new Identifier("my_mod", "main")); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-0-5) ...`

### Adding the first packet[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#adding-the-first-packet "Permanent link")

Packets sent using `OwoNetChannel` are declared as records - they're plain data-carriers. A simple packet might look like this:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-1-1) public record MyPacket(int someData, String otherData, Identifier aMinecraftClass) {}`

This now needs to be registered with your channel. To do this, you have two options:

*   #### Direct Registration[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#direct-registration "Permanent link")
    
    This needs to happen during general mod initialization (that is, most of the time in the class which implements `ModInitializer`) and is generally useful for packets which are either serverbound or whose handles don't reference client-only things in a way that would break a server.
    
    To register a packet in this style, use either the `registerClientbound` or `registerServerbound` method on your channel. These methods are named after where the packet is sent to, e.g. `registerServerbound` is used for packets sent _from_ the client _to_ the server.
    
    `[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-1) public class MyModInitializer implements ModInitializer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-3)     public static final OwoNetChannel MY_CHANNEL = OwoNetChannel.create(new Identifier("my_mod", "main")); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-5)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-6)     public void onInitialize() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-7)         MY_CHANNEL.registerServerbound(MyPacket.class, (message, access) -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-8)             // server-safe handler code goes here [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-9)         }); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-10)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-2-11) }`
    
      
    
*   #### Deferred Registration[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#deferred-registration "Permanent link")
    
    Same as direct registration, this has to happen during mod initialization. It may however, happen during different stages. This is useful for clientbound packets whose handles cannot be safely classloaded on a server.
    
    To register a packet in deferred mode, call `registerClientboundDeferred` during general mod initialization and `registerClientbound` during client mod initialization.
    
    General InitializerClient Initializer
    
    `[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-3-1) public class MyModInitializer implements ModInitializer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-3-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-3-3)     public static final OwoNetChannel MY_CHANNEL = OwoNetChannel.create(new Identifier("my_mod", "main")); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-3-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-3-5)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-3-6)     public void onInitialize() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-3-7)         MY_CHANNEL.registerClientboundDeferred(MyPacket.class); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-3-8)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-3-9) }`
    
    `[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-4-1) public class MyClientModInitializer implements ClientModInitializer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-4-2)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-4-3)     public void onInitializeClient() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-4-4)         MY_CHANNEL.registerClientbound(MyPacket.class, (message, access) -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-4-5)             // arbitrary handler code goes here [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-4-6)         }); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-4-7)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-4-8) }`
    

Now there are two important observations to be made about this code we just wrote:

1.  We did not write any serialization code, nor did we register any serializers. All primitives, a lot of Java utility classes and most if not all relevant Minecraft utility classes are supported out of the box
    
2.  Because serialization is done for us, we do not need to manually schedule our processing on the client or server thread - this is handled by the channel directly
    

You might also wonder what the two parameters in the handler represent. It's quite straight forward: `message` is simply the deserialized packet (a `MyPacket` instance in the example) and `access` is short for `EnvironmentAccess` - it lets you grab the player which received the packet as well as the client or server in the form of the `runtime` property.

### Sending the first packet[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#sending-the-first-packet "Permanent link")

In order to send a packet via an `OwoNetChannel`, you need what we call a `Handle`. This is an object bound to a certain target, with a `send` method which sends packets to that target. To bind and obtain a `Handle`, use either the `clientHandler()` or any of the `serverHandle(...)` methods. A handle is always named after where it is sending _from_, thus a `ServerHandle` sends _from_ the server _to_ the client and vice-versa.

Attention

The server and client handles are re-used. Each channel stores exactly one handle of each kind and binds it every time you request it via any of the methods. This means you _cannot_ store a handle for later usage - it is not in any way guaranteed to still be bound to the same target and could thus cause all kinds of weird and undefined behavior.

Once you obtained a handle, you can use it to send a packet:

Server ExampleClient Example

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-5-1) // to send to a certain player [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-5-2) var player = <some server player>; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-5-3) MyModInitializer.MY_CHANNEL.serverHandle(player).send(new MyPacket(1, "this", new Identifier("is", "podge"))); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-5-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-5-5) // to send to all players watching a block entity [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-5-6) var blockEntity = <some block entity>; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-5-7) MyModInitializer.MY_CHANNEL.serverHandle(blockEntity).send(new MyPacket(1, "this", new Identifier("is", "podge")));`

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#__codelineno-6-1) MyModInitializer.MY_CHANNEL.clientHandle().send(new MyPacket(1, "this", new Identifier("is", "podge")));`

* * *

Last update: 3 years ago2022-10-04

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/#)

---

# Registration - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#basics)

Registration
============

The further down this article goes, the more advanced it becomes and the less likely it is you will need the information for a simple mod.

Basics[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#basics "Permanent link")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

0.1.3

oωo offers a flexible system for automatically registering things into `Registry` instances. It revolves around the idea of storing the values to be registered into `public static` fields of a class. Consider this example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-1) public class ItemInit { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-3)     public static final Item BLACKBERRY = new Item(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-4)     public static final Item BANANA = new Item(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-5)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-7)     public static void init() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-8)         Registry.register(Registry.ITEM, Mod.id("blackberry"), BLACKBERRY); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-9)         Registry.register(Registry.ITEM, Mod.id("banana"), BANANA); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-10)         ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-11)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-12) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-0-13) }`

Because all this class does is register each of its fields into the `ITEM` registry, it can be easily shortened by implementing `ItemRegistryContainer`

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-1-1) public class ItemInit implements ItemRegistryContainer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-1-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-1-3)     public static final Item BLACKBERRY = new Item(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-1-4)     public static final Item BANANA = new Item(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-1-5)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-1-6)     public static final String notAnItem = "this will be ignored"; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-1-7)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-1-8) }`

As you can see, basically all boilerplate was eliminated and the code is now entirely declarative. Now you might be wondering when your items will be registered. Luckily, you still get to keep full control of that. Instead of calling `init()`, you now use the `FieldRegistrationHandler`.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-1) public class ModInit implements ModInitializer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-3)     public static final String MOD_ID = "based"; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-5)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-6)     public void onInitialize() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-7)         ... // before [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-8)         ItemInit.init(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-9)         ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-10) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-11)         ... // after [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-12)         FieldRegistrationHandler.register(ItemInit.class, MOD_ID, false); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-13)         ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-14)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-2-15) }`

All the fields of your `ItemInit` class will now be registered the moment you call this method. Their IDs will be determined by the name of the field prefixed with the namespace you passed to the handler - e.g. the `BANANA` in this example would be registered as `based:banana`. The sneaky `String` inside the `ItemInit` class will be ignored - in fact, any field that does not match or extend the type you're registering will be.

### Blocks[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#blocks "Permanent link")

Blocks are a bit of a special case because each block usually also requires a `BlockItem`. Conveniently, the `BlockRegistryContainer` takes care of that. You can just implement it without declaring any methods, however you won't get any control over the generated `BlockItem`s that way. As such, it is normally a good idea to also implement `createBlockItem(...)` in your class.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-1) public class BlockInit implements BlockRegistryContainer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-3)     public static final Block CLEAR_GLASS = new Block(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-5)     @NoBlockItem // available since 0.3.13+1.18 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-6)     public static final Block DEBUG_BLOCK = new Block(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-8)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-9)     public BlockItem createBlockItem(Block block, String identifier) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-10)         return new BlockItem(block, new Item.Settings().group(Mod.MOD_GROUP)); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-11)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-3-12) }`

As you can see, you get full control over the BlockItem which is created. You might also have noticed the `@NoBlockItem` annotation on the debug block. It simply tells the registration system that this specific block should not have an item created for it.

### Non-Standard types[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#non-standard-types "Permanent link")

Up to this point, we've been using the pre-defined implementations of `AutoRegistryContainer<T>` that oωo provides. These don't exist for all registries however, thus we need to make our own. Implementing this interface is trivial though, we only need to provide the type of field to register as well as the matching `Registry`.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-1) public class BlockEntityInit implements AutoRegistryContainer<BlockEntityType<?>> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-3)     public static final BlockEntityType<ModBlockEntity> MOD_BLOCK_ENTITY = FabricBlockEntityTypeBuilder.create(...).build(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-5)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-6)     public Registry<BlockEntityType<?>> getRegistry() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-7)         return Registry.BLOCK_ENTITY_TYPE; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-8)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-9) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-10)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-11)     @SuppressWarnings("unchecked") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-12)     public Class<BlockEntityType<?>> getTargetFieldType() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-13)         return (Class<BlockEntityType<?>>) (Object) BlockEntityType.class; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-14)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-4-15) }`

You may notice that there is some nasty casting going on inside `getTargetFieldType()`. You can safely copy and ignore it should you need it yourself, it is simply here to talk the compiler into doing its job.

### Running extra work after registration[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#running-extra-work-after-registration "Permanent link")

Should you have some work you would have usually executed at the end of you `init()` method, you can implement the `afterFieldProcessing()` method on your container class.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-5-1) public class BlockInit implements BlockRegistryContainer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-5-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-5-3)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-5-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-5-5)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-5-6)     public void afterFieldProcessing() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-5-7)         // do extra work here [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-5-8)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-5-9) }`

Advanced Usage[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#advanced-usage "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Annotations[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#annotations "Permanent link")

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-6-1) @AssignedName`

This annotation may be used if you wish your field to have a different name than the one it has in code. Refer to this example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-7-1) public class ItemInit implements ItemRegistryContainer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-7-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-7-3)     public static final Item BANANA = new Item(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-7-4)     // registered as 'mod_id:banana' [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-7-5) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-7-6)     @AssignedName("apple") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-7-7)     public static final Item ORANGE = new Item(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-7-8)     // registered as 'mod_id:apple' instead of 'mod_id:orange' [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-7-9) }`

* * *

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-8-1) @IterationIgnored`

Signals the `FieldRegistrationHandler` that the annotated field should be ignored when processing the class. Refer to this example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-9-1) public class ItemInit implements ItemRegistryContainer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-9-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-9-3)     public static final Item BANANA = new Item(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-9-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-9-5)     @IterationIgnored [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-9-6)     public static final Item NOT_REGISTERED = new Item(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-9-7) }`

### Inner classes[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#inner-classes "Permanent link")

Should you want to organize your container class with subclasses, you're in luck as the system fully supports this scheme. In fact, there is an intended use-case - registering fields into different namespaces. To make use of this, create an inner class which implements the same type of registry container as the outer one. Then, annotate it with the `@RegistryNamespace` annotation to override the namespace of the generated identifiers.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-1) public class ItemInit implements ItemRegistryContainer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-3)     // registered as 'mod_id:banana' [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-4)     public static final Item BANANA = new Item(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-5) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-6)     @RegistryNamespace("inner_class") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-7)     public static class Inner implements ItemRegistryContainer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-8) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-9)         // registered as 'inner_class:damascus_ingot' [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-10)         public static final Item DAMASCUS_INGOT = new Item(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-11)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-10-12) }`

Finally, to make this work, change the last argument in the call to `FieldRegistrationHandler.register(...)` to `true`. This tells it to also search the inner classes of the target class, which we usually keep disabled.

### Non-registry targets[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#non-registry-targets "Permanent link")

As the field-traversal system used by the `AutoRegistryContainer<T>` is generic and exposed as part of oωo's API, you can also use to iterate the fields of something non-registry related.

Say, for example, you had a class which does many complex things and that needs to be initialized. Further imagine you had multiple instances of it stored in the fields of a container class. You could then implement `SimpleFieldProcessingSubject<T>` on that container class and initialize them all at once.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-1) public class ComplexInit implements SimpleFieldProcessingSubject<ComplexThing> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-3)     public static final ComplexThing A_COMPLEX_THING = new ComplexThing(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-4)     public static final ComplexThing ANOTHER_COMPLEX_THING = new ComplexThing(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-5)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-7)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-8)     public void processField(ComplexThing thing, String identifier, Field field) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-9)         thing.init(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-10)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-11) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-12)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-13)     public Class<ComplexThing> getTargetFieldType() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-14)         return ComplexThing.class; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-15)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-11-16) }`

To then execute this code, simply use the `FieldRegistrationHandler`

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-12-1) FieldRegistrationHandler.processSimple(ComplexInit.class, false);`

For further information on how this system works and what it can do, take a look at the [javadoc](https://docs.wispforest.io/javadoc/owo/io/wispforest/owo/registration/reflect/package-summary.html)
 for the `io.wispforest.owo.registration.reflect` package.

### Determining block item settings with annotations[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#determining-block-item-settings-with-annotations "Permanent link")

0.3.13+1.18

Sometimes, you might want to change the `Item.Settings` of a block item only for some blocks in your `BlockRegistryContainer`. If this applies to one or two of them, a simple `if (...)` in the `createBlockItem` method should suffice, but if a more flexible system is desired you can override `postProcessField(...)` in your container class.

This method has a default implementation that simply calls `createBlockItem`, but we won't do that anymore and instead directly create the item in there. This has the advantage of having the `Field` object available, so annotation lookups are possible. First, let's define our annotation, in its own class file:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-13-1) @Retention(RetentionPolicy.RUNTIME) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-13-2) @Target(ElementType.FIELD) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-13-3) public @interface NoItemGroup {}`

This is just a simple annotation with no value that can only applied to a field and that is retained for runtime-access, unlike the default `SOURCE` policy.

We can then use it to annotate a field and check for its presence in our overridden `postProcessField(...)` method.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-1) public class BlockInit implements BlockRegistryContainer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-3)     public static final Block CLEAR_GLASS = new Block(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-5)     @NoItemGroup [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-6)     public static final Block DEBUG_BLOCK = new Block(...); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-8)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-9)     public void postProcessField(String namespace, Block value, String identifier, Field field) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-10)         // preserve normal traversal behaviour [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-11)         if (field.isAnnotationPresent(NoBlockItem.class)) return; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-12) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-13)         // create basic item settings [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-14)         var settings = new Item.Settings(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-15) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-16)         // check if our annotation is present and only  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-17)         // assign the itemgroup if it is not [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-18)         if (!field.isAnnotationPresent(NoItemGroup.class)){ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-19)             settings.group(Mod.MOD_GROUP) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-20)         } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-21) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-22)         // finally, create and register the block item [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-23)         Registry.register(Registry.ITEM, new Identifier(namespace, identifier), new BlockItem(value, settings))); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-24)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#__codelineno-14-25) }`

This is only a simple example, although it should make it clear how this system can be expanded to cover more of the items' properties.

* * *

Last update: 3 years ago2023-01-29

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/registration/#)
