# Getting Started - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#basics)

Getting Started
===============

### Basics[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#basics "Permanent link")

In order to use owo-config, you need to have the relevant annotation processor active in your build environment. To do this, edit the dependency (from [setup](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/setup/)
):

build.gradle

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-1) dependencies { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-2)     annotationProcessor modImplementation("io.wispforest:owo-lib:${project.owo_version}") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-3) }`

* * *

The first step to creating your config is making a config model class. This class describes the structure of your config, but is never interacted with directly. Instead, you simply apply the `@Config` annotation and the annotation processor takes care of the rest.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-1) @Config(name = "my-config", wrapperName = "MyConfig") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-2) public class MyConfigModel { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-3)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-4) }`

As you can see, this annotation accepts two attributes - both of which are equally important.

*   `name` is the filename under which your config is saved, as well the identifier that's used when your config is sent over the network
    
*   `wrapperName` is the name of the actual config class which will get generated. This is the class which you interact with to load your config and pass it around, so choose something sensible
    

You can now add options to your config. To do that, simply add fields to your class.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-1) @Config(name = "my-config", wrapperName = "MyConfig") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-2) public class MyConfigModel { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-3)     public int anIntOption = 16; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-4)     public boolean aBooleanToggle = false; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-5) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-6)     public Choices anEnumOption = Choices.ANOTHER_CHOICE; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-8)     public enum Choices { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-9)         A_CHOICE, ANOTHER_CHOICE; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-10)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-11) }`

After you're done adding your first options, it's time to build your project once. This runs the annotation processor and will generate the wrapper class, ready to use. Once this has completed, load the config in your mod initializer:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-1) public class MyModInitializer implements ModInitializer { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-2)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-3)     public static final MyConfig CONFIG = MyConfig.createAndLoad(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-4)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-5) }`

Note for Eclipse IDE users

If you are using Eclipse IDE, you will need to do some additional configuration to get the generated class to register. In your build.gradle, add the following:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-1) sourceSets.main.java.srcDirs += [ 'src/main/generatedJava' ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-2) compileJava.options.generatedSourceOutputDirectory = file("${projectDir}/src/main/generatedJava/<your config class package>")`

This will ensure that the generated class ends up the correct directory, and that it gets picked up by Eclipse. Just make sure to replace `<your config class package>` with the path of your `ConfigModel`'s package. For example if your `ConfigModel` class is at: `com.example.config.MyConfigModel`, you would use `com/example/config`.

And that's it! You can now use your config values everywhere.

#### Additional options[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#additional-options "Permanent link")

The `@Config` annotation provides two additional parameters - `defaultHook` as well as `saveOnModification`.

*   `defaultHook` defaults to `false` and declares whether all of your config options should be treated like they were annotated with [`@Hook`](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#hook)
     - that is, have a method to register callbacks
    
*   `saveOnModification` defaults to `true` and tells the config whether it should automatically save itself whenever any of the options are changed
    

#### Translations[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#translations "Permanent link")

Each option's translation key is generated based on its key as well as the config it resides in. The generated keys take the form `text.config.<config name>.option.<option key>`. To add a tooltip to an option, simply add a translation for the `text.config.<config name>.option.<option key>.tooltip` key, it will automatically show up. This translation supports `\n` line breaks for formatting the tooltip.

Translation keys for enums are generated based on the name of the option, like this: `text.config.<config name>.option.<option key>.value.<name of enum value>`. The name of the enum value is always fully lowercase.

#### Registering with [ModMenu](https://modrinth.com/mod/modmenu)
[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#registering-with-modmenu "Permanent link")

![modmenu config example](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/config-modmenu.png) In order to make your config screen available from ModMenu, you only need to apply the `@Modmenu` annotation to your config model class.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-1) @Modmenu(modId = "mymodid") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-2) @Config(name = "my-config", wrapperName = "MyConfig") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-3) public class MyConfigModel { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-4)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-5) }`

The annotation requires that you pass in your mod's id, and optionally a custom UI model. This UI model is the XML file that's used for generating the config screen - customizing this file is the easiest way to customize your config screen.

### Organizing the config screen[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#organizing-the-config-screen "Permanent link")

When your config has more than just a few options, it is often beneficial to organize it in a sensible manner. owo-config provides two tools for this purpose - sections and nested objects

#### Sections[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#sections "Permanent link")

![section header example](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/config-section-header.png) A section gets a header as shown above and can also be quickly navigated to using the sidebar. To begin a new section in your config, simply apply the `@SectionHeader` annotation to the field with which you want the section to begin.

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-1) @Config(name = "my-config", wrapperName = "MyConfig") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-2) public class MyConfigModel { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-3)     public String firstOption = "1"; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-4)     ... // many more options [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-5) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-6)     @SectionHeader("someSection") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-7)     public String someLaterOption = "42"; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-8) }`

#### Nested Objects[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#nested-objects "Permanent link")

![nested object example](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/config-nested-object.png) A nested object adds a level of indentation to all the options inside it. It can also be collapsed to be out of the way if the options it contains are rarely needed. To define a nested object, declare an inner class in your config model, add a field of its type and apply the `@Nest` annotation to said field.

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-1) @Config(name = "my-config", wrapperName = "MyConfig") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-2) public class MyConfigModel { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-3)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-5)     @Nest [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-6)     public ThisIsNested nestedObject = new ThisIsNested(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-8)     public static class ThisIsNested { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-9)         public boolean aNestedValue = false; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-10)         public int anotherNestedValue = 42; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-11)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-12) }`

* * *

Last update: 2023-08-19

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/getting-started/#)

---

# Annotations - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#expanded)

Annotations
===========

Most of owo-config's features are enabled via annotations. The ones which aren't covered in other articles already are outlined on this page.

* * *

### `@Expanded`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#expanded "Permanent link")

This annotation applies to fields which are either a nested object or some sort of `List<T>` and makes them start expanded in the config screen.

* * *

### `@Hook`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#hook "Permanent link")

This annotation applies to any field and declares that a callback registrar[1](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#fn:1)
 should be generated. Refer to this handy example:

Config ModelGenerated Wrapper

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-0-1) @Config(name = "my-config", wrapperName = "MyConfig") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-0-2) public class MyConfigModel { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-0-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-0-4)     public int withoutHook = 0; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-0-5) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-0-6)     @Hook [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-0-7)     public int withHook = 1; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-0-8) }`

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-1-1) public class MyConfig extends ConfigWrapper<MyConfigModel> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-1-2)     ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-1-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-1-4)     public int withoutHook() {...} [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-1-5)     public void withoutHook(int value) {...} [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-1-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-1-7)     public int withHook() {...} [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-1-8)     public void withHook(int value) {...} [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-1-9)     public subscribeToWithHook(Consumer<Integer> subscriber) {...} [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#__codelineno-1-10) }`

* * *

### `@ExcludeFromScreen`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#excludefromscreen "Permanent link")

This annotation applies to any field and simply hides it from the config screen - this is useful if the option is either internal or has no support in the config screen and you want to suppress the warning.

* * *

### `@RestartRequired`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#restartrequired "Permanent link")

This annotation applies to any field and declares that the option it represents only actually applies after a restart of the game. The config screen indicates this and the player is explicitly notified when they close the screen.

The annotation also has a secondary effect when combined with `@Sync(Option.SyncMode.OVERRIDE_CLIENT)`. Because an option which only applies after restart cannot be dynamically overridden by the server, owo-config will not allow players to connect if their client's value does not match the server.

![config mismatch example](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/config-sync-error.png)

* * *

1.  Yes, this is a word [↩](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#fnref:1 "Jump back to footnote 1 in the text")
    

* * *

Last update: 2023-06-23

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/annotations/#)

---

# Constraints - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#regexconstraint)

Constraints
===========

There are three types of constraints you can put on your config options to declare which values are acceptable. If an option's value does not match its constraint during loading, it will be reset to its default value. If you try to apply an invalid value via code, the option will remain unchanged.

* * *

### `@RegexConstraint`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#regexconstraint "Permanent link")

This type of constraint applies to `String` config options and allows values which match the given regular expression

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-0-1) @RegexConstraint("[a-z]{1,10}") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-0-2) public String aStringOption = "matched";`

* * *

### `@RangeConstraint`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#rangeconstraint "Permanent link")

This type of constraint applies to numeric options and allows values which are between `min` and `max`, both _inclusive_

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-1-1) @RangeConstraint(min = 10, max = 20) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-1-2) public int anIntOption = 16; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-1-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-1-4) @RangeConstraint(min = 5.5d, max = 11.3d) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-1-5) public double aDoubleOption = 7.5;`

* * *

### `@PredicateConstraint`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#predicateconstraint "Permanent link")

This type of constraint applies to any field and allows values which match the given predicate function. You declare said function as a `static` method on your config model class and pass its name into the annotation.

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-1) @Config(...) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-2) public class MyConfigModel { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-4)     // we want to only allow lists of length 5 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-5)     @PredicateConstraint("predicateFunction") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-6)     public List<String> someOption = new ArrayList<>(List.of("1", "2", "3", "4", "5")); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-8)     // so we declare a predicate method [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-9)     public static boolean predicateFunction(List<String> list) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-10)         // and do the check in here [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-11)         // this could be arbitrarily complex code, but [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-12)         // we'll keep it simple for this demonstration [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-13)         return list.size() == 5; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-14)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-15) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#__codelineno-2-16) }`

* * *

Last update: 2022-10-04

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/constraints/#)

# owo-ui - Wisp Forest Docs

 

owo-ui
======

Work-in-progress

The owo-ui documentation is still being written and not quite complete yet. In places where an article here is still missing, you can always refer to the JavaDoc present throughout the library - it explains most things in detail

0.8.0

owo-ui is a declarative UI framework that helps with building dynamic screens quickly and easily. It strives to be highly embeddable, performant and, most of all, super easy to use. We provide the following major features:

*    **A simple Component tree**
    
    Every part of your UI is represented as one or multiple Components, which you compose in a simple tree structure - just like modern web tech
    
*    **Low-code UI design**
    
    You can choose to describe your layout in code or alternatively in a custom format implemented through standard XML. When using the XML-based approach, you essentially get hotswapping for free - when in dev-mode the file is reloaded every time you open the screen, making for blazingly fast iteration times
    
*    **A great developer experience**
    
    We strive to keep every part of the framework documented and provide an interactive tutorial ([owo-ui-academy](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/academy/)
    ) which teaches you the basics. While developing, you can easily debug your UI using the always-available component inspector, which works quite similarly to the "Inspect element" tool in modern browsers
    
*    **Robust Layout Engines**
    
    You rarely need to hardcode the position or size of a component - everything is computed dynamically to match current layout and available screen space
    
*    **Easy Animations**
    
    Even the most functional of screens can use a little animation now and then - owo-ui got you covered. Animating the size or position of a component over time is as simple as calling a single function
    

* * *

Last update: 2022-10-04

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/#)

# Synchronization - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/synchronization/#the-concept)

Synchronization
===============

The Concept[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/synchronization/#the-concept "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The majority of your config options are usually only used on one side - either the client or the server. Sometimes though, a server-side option may also affect client-side behavior in certain superficial ways, or it may even be strictly required that the client and server values match up. For these cases, owo-config supports server-client config synchronization - either for single values or even your entire config.

Implementation[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/synchronization/#implementation "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To enable config sync, simply apply the `@Sync` annotation to the option you want synchronized. When doing this, it is worth noting that the annotation cascades - that is, it applies to every option (or rather field) nested inside the one it was applied to as well. However, a more specific application always take priority - say you have sync enabled on your config class, you can then disable it for individual options and their children by applying the annotation to them again.

### Sync Modes[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/synchronization/#sync-modes "Permanent link")

*   `Option.SyncMode.NONE`: Quite self-explanatory, this is the default and makes it so the option is never synchronized in any way.
    
*   `Option.SyncMode.INFORM_SERVER`: This sync mode only sends the client's value to the server for later use via `ConfigSynchronizer.getClientOptions(...)`, but not the other way around.
    
*   `Option.SyncMode.OVERRIDE_CLIENT`: Send the server's value to the client and temporarily override the client's value. Enabling `OVERRIDE_CLIENT` implies `INFORM_SERVER`
    

Option Serialization

To send your config's value over the network, owo's networking stack is employed - specifically the `PacketBufSerializer` system. It _should_ support all commonly used types out-of-the box, yet it is not impossible to think of a situation where you may need a custom serializer. For those cases, simply call `PacketBufSerializer.register(...)` **before** you load your config and provide the necessary code.

### Detached Options[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/synchronization/#detached-options "Permanent link")

When a client-side option gets overridden by the server, it enters the so-called "detached" state. In this state, it is essentially a dangling container for a value without any relation to its backing field. It will not get serialized when the config gets saved and any attempt made at modifying its value will fail. Should the player open the config screen while on a server, the option will appear as "managed by the server" and cannot be edited.

### Restart-only options[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/synchronization/#restart-only-options "Permanent link")

When `@Sync(Option.SyncMode.OVERRIDE_CLIENT)` is applied to a field which is also annotated as `@RestartRequired`, special handling is employed. Because such a value cannot be safely overridden by the server, the server's value is instead only used for verification. In case the client's value _does not match the server_, the client will automatically disconnect and prompt the user to change the value themselves and restart.

![config mismatch example](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/config-sync-error.png)

Config Sync Flow[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/synchronization/#config-sync-flow "Permanent link")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

    graph LR
      A[Server] -->|Send values| B{Unrecoverable<br>Mismatch?};
      B -->|No| C((Connected));
      style C stroke:#00FFAB,stroke-width:4px
    
      C --> E[Respond with <br> local values];
      B --x|Yes| D[Connection <br>  aborted]; 
      style D stroke:#FF4949,stroke-width:4px

* * *

Last update: 2023-06-23

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/config/synchronization/#)

# owo-ui Academy - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/academy/#setup)

owo-ui Academy
==============

![owo-ui-academy example screen](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/ui-academy.png)

owo-ui-academy is an interactive, in-game tutorial that teaches you the essential concepts of owo-ui.

#### Setup[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/academy/#setup "Permanent link")

Given that it is a developer tool, builds are not publicly hosted - you need to get them from [GitHub Actions](https://github.com/wisp-forest/owo-ui-academy/actions)
. Alternatively you may also clone the repository and run it, just like any other mod.

Once you have the mod installed, simply join a world and press the keybind helpfully noted in the little notification.

#### Using the Inspector[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/academy/#using-the-inspector "Permanent link")

While playing around with owo-ui-academy, the inspector is your most important tool. It can visualize what's internally going on in the playground and also how the tutorial screens themselves are laid out. Apart from the standard inspector, you can also press Alt+Shift to bring it into _global mode_, where it will draw the debug overlay for every component on screen.

* * *

# Component Basics - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/component-basics/#using-the-inspector)

Component Basics
================

There are quite a few things to know about how components internally work and how their properties decide behavior. This page serves as a helpful reference for the most important concepts.

Using the Inspector[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/component-basics/#using-the-inspector "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Many properties of a component can be analyzed visually right in game, using the component inspector. While in debug mode, it can be enabled on any owo screen (or, more specifically, any UI adapter which can capture the relevant keyboard input) by pressing Ctrl+Shift. You can then use your mouse to hover the component you wish to inspect. The text annotation presents information in the following format:

![inspector text format](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/inspector-reference.png)

The type of the component  
The ID of the component (if defined)  
The absolute coordinates of the component  
The actual size of the component  
The margins of the component: `<top,bottom,left,right>`  
The padding of the component (only on parent components)

Everything is given in logical pixels - that is, pixels after the UI Scale option is applied. If you wish the see the bounding boxes and margins of the entire UI tree, press Alt+Shift to bring the inspector into global mode.

Margins[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/component-basics/#margins "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![margins explainer image](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/margins-reference.png)

Each component defines a set of margins. These decide how much dead space to add around the component's main bounding box on each side - this is most often useful for spacing out neighboring components. Margins may also be negative, which effectively shrinks the bounding box of the component on that side, although results may sometimes be counterintuitive.

The inspector draws the margins of a component in bright yellow

Padding[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/component-basics/#padding "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

![padding explainer image](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/padding-reference.png)

Every parent component defines padding. This decides how much dead space is added inside the component's bounding box, surrounding its children. If the component is not content-sized, this means the space available to its children becomes smaller. Just like margins, padding may be negative.

The inspector draws the padding of a component in bright cyan

Sizing[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/component-basics/#sizing "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The sizing of a component describes how its size should be calculated. There are three methods available, which you can apply independently on both axes:

*   **Content** | `method="content"` `Sizing.content()`
    
    A content-sized component is always as large as it needs to be to fit all of its content (plus some amount of padding, which you can specify). Not all components support this method, as they may not have an intrinsic size, and will throw an exception when configured this way.
    
*   **Fill** | `method="fill"` `Sizing.fill(...)`
    
    Fill-sizing dynamically makes the component fill the given percentage of the available space. If the parent of this component is content-sized, this means the available space will the that of the parent. If all parents are content-sized, the entire screen is regarded as available.
    
*   **Fixed** | `method="fixed"` `Sizing.fixed(...)`
    
    Fixed simply hard-defines the size of the component in pixels
    

Positioning[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/component-basics/#positioning "Permanent link")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The positioning of a component describes how it should be placed on the screen. Just as with sizing, there are three different types available:

*   **Layout** | `type="layout"` `Positioning.layout()`
    
    Layout positioning declares that this component wishes to be part of its parent's layout. This is a unique property - components with absolute and relative positioning are ignored during the layout process and always placed on the screen according to their positioning.
    
*   **Relative** | `type="relative"` `Positioning.relative(...)`
    
    A relatively positioning component gets placed the specified percentage across the parent - _including the component's own size_. This means that 50|50 makes the component centered and 100|100 pushes it all the way into the bottom right corner, but values between 0 and 100 can never make a component overflow
    
*   **Absolute** | `type="absolute"` `Positioning.absolute(...)`
    
    Absolute positioning is the most straight-forward - it simply places the component at the specified amount of pixels offset from the parent's origin.
    

* * *

Last update: 2023-06-23

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/component-basics/#)

---

# Layout Basics - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/layout-basics/#layout-types)

Layout Basics
=============

When building a UI, arranging components on screen is one of your primary tasks - in owo-ui, this is accomplished using layout components. A layout component is a parent component which accepts multiple children and places them on the screen in a certain fashion.

Layout Types[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/layout-basics/#layout-types "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

owo-ui has two built-in layout components, which we'll explore now. Should neither of these meet your needs, you can always make your own - simply extend `BaseParentComponent`.

### Flow Layout[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/layout-basics/#flow-layout "Permanent link")

![vertical flow layout reference](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/flow-layout-reference.png)

`<flow-layout direction="vertical|​horizontal">`  
`Containers.verticalFlow(...)` | `Containers.horizontalFlow(...)`

The flow layout is the simplest layout you could possibly think of - as the name suggests, it simply places all children one after the other. Depending on the axis, components flow top-to-bottom or left-to-right in the order that they were added.

### Grid Layout[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/layout-basics/#grid-layout "Permanent link")

`<grid-layout rows="..." columns="...">`  
`Containers.grid(...)`

The grid layout is equally simple as the flow layout - it places every child in its own cell of a grid. The amount of rows and columns must be defined when you create the layout, as it internally represent the grid as a fixed-size array.

When a grid layout is content-sized, every row and column becomes as large as it needs to be to fit the largest cell. Otherwise, every row and column is evenly split along the layout's length in that direction.

![grid layout reference](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/grid-layout-reference.png)

Layout Properties[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/layout-basics/#layout-properties "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Every layout (in fact, all parent components) share some additional properties which normal components don't define. The ones relevant to layout are listed here.

### Alignment[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/layout-basics/#alignment "Permanent link")

The horizontal and vertical alignment of a parent component dictates where within itself the children should be positioned. For most components this is relative to the whole component, however the grid is an exception to this - children are always aligned relative to their respective cell.

### Padding[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/layout-basics/#padding "Permanent link")

As explained in [component basics](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/component-basics/#padding)
, all parent components define padding which is removed from the area available to their children. This is most useful in combination with a Surface, as it means you can add some extra visual breathing room around the children and make the border of your surface clearly visible.

### Overflow Clipping[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/layout-basics/#overflow-clipping "Permanent link")

While playing around with the framework, you may have encountered a situation under which a child component extends outside its parent without the protruding parts actually being rendered. This is due to overflow clipping - by default all parent components only allow rendering inside their bounding box. You can of course disable this and allow overflow to be rendered, although that generally leads to more problems than it solves.

A child which is completely invisible due to this is skipped entirely during rendering, which majorly improves performance with large scroll containers.

* * *

Last update: 2023-06-23

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/layout-basics/#)

---

# Getting Started - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#choosing-a-paradigm)

Getting Started
===============

Choosing a paradigm[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#choosing-a-paradigm "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Before creating your first screen with owo-ui, you need to decide which approach you want to take: code-driven or data-driven. Here's a quick comparison:

| [Code-driven](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#code-driven) | [Data-driven](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#data-driven) |
| --- | --- |
| **+** Everything in one place: your logic and  <br>layout reside in a single file | **+** Superior, more readable  <br>visual structure |
| **+** Slightly faster to set up | **+** Can be changed by resource packs |
| **\-** Hotswapping can be slow | **+** Instant reloading |
|     | **\-** Slightly more hassle to maintain |

In general, the code-driven approach is recommended for beginners. However, it is often preferable to switch to data-driven UI design once you're more familiar with the framework.

While there is currently no tool for converting between the two paradigms, it's usually pretty easy to rewrite your UI in either of them - so don't worry too much about the decision you make here.

### Code-driven[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#code-driven "Permanent link")

In order to begin building your first screen with the code-driven approach, create a screen class which extends `BaseOwoScreen`. You will notice that this superclass requires a type parameter - this is the type of root component you want to use. Since we're just starting out, let's pick the `FlowLayout` and implement the `createAdapter()` and `build(...)` methods.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-1) public class MyFirstScreen extends BaseOwoScreen<FlowLayout> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-3)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-4)     protected @NotNull OwoUIAdapter<FlowLayout> createAdapter() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-5)         // TODO [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-6)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-8)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-9)     protected void build(FlowLayout rootComponent) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-10)         // TODO [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-11)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-12) }`

You now need to fill in these two methods. In `createAdapter()` you have to initialize the UI system. For this job we use `OwoUIAdapter.create(...)` and pass in the screen and root component factory[1](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#fn:1)
, for which we'll choose the `FlowLayout` with the `VERTICAL` algorithm via `Containers.verticalFlow(...)`, making the final implementation look like this:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-1) @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-2) protected @NotNull OwoUIAdapter<FlowLayout> createAdapter() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-3)     return OwoUIAdapter.create(this, Containers::verticalFlow); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-4) }`

About the UI Adapter

The UI Adapter is the primary entrypoint to using owo-ui. It handles input events, rendering the component tree, initiating layout inflation, and most importantly it implements all interfaces required to function as a vanilla widget. This means that adding owo-ui to an existing screen can easily be done by creating an adapter and `addDrawableChild`ing it. This isn't a requirement however - the fact that you can use this one handle to utilize the entire UI system is the main reason it is as embeddable as it is. In general: If you have a 2D rendering context, you can use owo-ui.

And that's it! You now have the screen all initialized and ready to go. If you open it at this point, you'll see precisely nothing:

![a blank screen](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/getting-started/step-0.png)

Let's fix that by giving our root component a so-called surface, in this case the standard dark, translucent background most vanilla UIs use.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-1) @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-2) protected void build(FlowLayout rootComponent) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-3)     rootComponent.surface(Surface.VANILLA_TRANSLUCENT); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-4) }`

About Surfaces

Every parent component (that is, every component which can contain other components) has what's called a "Surface" which is in charge of rendering the component's background. There are several defaults available to use directly on the `Surface` interface which should cover most bases, and all surfaces can be chained using the `and(...)` method. Should you require a more custom solution however, simply provide your surface as a lambda - it's only a rendering function after all.

Now the screen looks like this:

![a screen with a dark translucent background](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/getting-started/step-1.png)

Great! Let's begin by simply adding a button right in the center. To accomplish this, we first set the root component's alignment to `CENTER` on both axes and then add our button - like this:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-1) @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-2) protected void build(FlowLayout rootComponent) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-3)     rootComponent [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-4)                 .surface(Surface.VANILLA_TRANSLUCENT) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-5)                 .horizontalAlignment(HorizontalAlignment.CENTER) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-6)                 .verticalAlignment(VerticalAlignment.CENTER); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-8)     rootComponent.child( [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-9)         Components.button( [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-10)                 Text.literal("A Button"),  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-11)                 button -> { System.out.println("click"); } // (1) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-12)             ) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-13)     ); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-14) }`

1.  Here we tell the button what do when pressed - in this case it just prints something to the console

Component type decay

While writing this code you probably noticed that all the methods we're calling on the root component return the component, so we can easily chain calls. You may even have tried to append the `.child(...)` call after the alignment has been set up, but couldn't because the method suddenly did not exist anymore. This is due to type decay - methods on components will always return the least specific type of component they're defined on. Because alignment is a property common to all parent components, the method returns precisely that - a `ParentComponent` instead of a `FlowLayout`, which does not define a way to add children. You will encounter this often, so remember that you can simply avoid it by changing the order of your method calls.

The result is as expected, a button saying "A Button" right in the center of our screen:

![a screen with a centered button](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/getting-started/step-2.png)

Before we finish off this introduction, let's wrap the button in a container and style that like a vanilla UI panel. To do this, we only need to create the container via `Containers.verticalFlow(...)` and add our button and surface to it like normal. If you understood everything so far, the following code should be pretty simple to grasp:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-1) @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-2) protected void build(FlowLayout rootComponent) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-3)     rootComponent [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-4)                 .surface(Surface.VANILLA_TRANSLUCENT) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-5)                 .horizontalAlignment(HorizontalAlignment.CENTER) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-6)                 .verticalAlignment(VerticalAlignment.CENTER); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-8)     rootComponent.child( [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-9)             Containers.verticalFlow(Sizing.content() /*(1)*/, Sizing.content()) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-10)                 .child(Components.button(Text.literal("A Button"), button -> { System.out.println("click"); })) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-11)                 .padding(Insets.of(10)) // (2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-12)                 .surface(Surface.DARK_PANEL) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-13)                 .verticalAlignment(VerticalAlignment.CENTER) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-14)                 .horizontalAlignment(HorizontalAlignment.CENTER) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-15)     ); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-4-16) }`

1.  When creating the container we need to tell it how large it's supposed to be. By providing `Sizing.content()` for both axes we tell it to make itself however large it needs to be to fit its children
    
2.  In order to properly see the surface of our container, we must make it slightly larger than the button - we do this by giving it 10 pixels of padding on all sides
    

Leaving us with a final screen that looks like this:

![a screen with a centered button and a panel around it](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/getting-started/step-3.png)

### Data-driven[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#data-driven "Permanent link")

Before jumping in the XML-based approach, let's clear up some terminology. The XML file which we're about to make is called the **UI Model**, since it describes a UI. It contains your component tree and, optionally, **templates** which can be used for creating similar components with different parameters.

To create your first screen in this fashion, extend `BaseUIModelScreen`. Just like `BaseOwoScreen` it expects a type parameter describing which kind of root component you want to use. Since we're trying to create the same screen we did with the code-driven approach, we'll specify `FlowLayout`.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-1) public class MyScreen extends BaseUIModelScreen<FlowLayout> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-3)     public MyScreen() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-4)         super(FlowLayout.class, /* TODO */); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-5)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-7)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-8)     protected void build(FlowLayout rootComponent) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-9)         // TODO [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-10)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-5-11) }`

Now the superclass constructor requires a `DataSource`. This is simply a way to describe where the UI Model should be loaded from - for this there are two standard options:

*   ~`DataSource.file(...)` is used for development - you simply give it the file path to your UI model, relative to the game's run directory. With this data source, the file is re-loaded every time you open the screen, which enables the instant hotswapping. When building for production however, this is not an option and will crash at runtime.~  
      
    As of **0.11**, this is deprecated and should no longer be used. Instead, you can press Ctrl+F5 while viewing the screen and select your UI model file in the menu that shows. Alternatively, you can also use the `/owo-ui-set-reload-path` command to associated a file with any given UI model
    
*   `DataSource.asset(...)` loads the model from the current resourcepacks. It expects an identifier like `mymod:my_ui_model`, which would point to `assets/mymod/owo_ui/my_ui_model.xml`. This way the model is only refreshed when reloading resource packs, making for much better performance and allowing resourcepacks to override and customize your UI.
    

For this example, let's use the `assets` data source and place our `my_ui_model.xml` file in th `assets/mymod/owo_ui/` directory of your project, turning the constructor into this:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-1) public MyScreen() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-2)     super(FlowLayout.class, DataSource.asset(new Identifier("mymod", "my_ui_model"))); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-6-3) }`

Now comes the meat of this exercise - creating the UI Model in XML. To begin, we'll create a file called `my_ui_model.xml` in the run directory, with the following content:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-1) <owo-ui xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-2)         xsi:noNamespaceSchemaLocation="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wisp-forest/owo-lib/1.20/owo-ui.xsd"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-3)     <components> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-5)     </components> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-7-6) </owo-ui>`

If you're using IntelliJ, you now have to place your cursor on the URL in `xsi:noNamespaceSchemaLocation`, press Alt+Enter and select `Fetch external resource`. This will make it download the XML schema, giving you rich autocomplete and error checking right inside the IDE.

Great, you can now begin building your UI. Let's first declare the root component. We'll use the `flow-layout`, just as declared on our class, and say that its `direction` is `vertical`: ![flow layout in xml](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/owo/getting-started/flow-layout.gif)

We're now again at the point were you can open your screen - once again it will just be completely blank. Let's add content then - for the sake of brevity this will now all be a single code block:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-1) <owo-ui xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-2)         xsi:noNamespaceSchemaLocation="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wisp-forest/owo-lib/1.20/owo-ui.xsd"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-3)     <components> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-4)         <flow-layout direction="vertical"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-5)             <children> <!--(1)--> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-6)                 <flow-layout direction="vertical"> <!--(2)--> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-7)                     <children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-8)                         <button id="the-button"> <!--(3)--> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-9)                             <text>A Button</text> <!--(6)--> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-10)                         </button> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-11)                     </children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-12) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-13)                     <horizontal-alignment>center</horizontal-alignment> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-14)                     <vertical-alignment>center</vertical-alignment> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-15) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-16)                     <!--(4)--> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-17)                     <padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-18)                         <all>10</all> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-19)                     </padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-20) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-21)                     <surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-22)                         <panel dark="true"/> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-23)                     </surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-24)                 </flow-layout> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-25)             </children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-26) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-27)             <vertical-alignment>center</vertical-alignment> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-28)             <horizontal-alignment>center</horizontal-alignment> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-29) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-30)             <!--(5)--> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-31)             <surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-32)                 <vanilla-translucent/> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-33)             </surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-34)         </flow-layout> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-35)     </components> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-8-36) </owo-ui>`

1.  This is where you declare the children of the flow layout - much like calling `.child(...)` in the previous example
    
2.  Here, we declare the container for the button - this is the equivalent of `Containers.verticalFlow(...)`
    
3.  Here goes the button itself. As you can see, we give it an ID - this will be important soon
    
4.  We declare padding very similarly to how it's done it code - note however, that these declarations like `all` can chain. This means if you want 5 pixels on the bottom and 10 everywhere else, you could simply append `<bottom>5</bottom>` into the `padding` element
    
5.  Surfaces work in much the same way as they do in code. The only difference is that they automatically chain - if you were to add `<panel/>` before the `<vanilla-translucent/>` you'd get a vanilla panel under a dark rectangle
    
6.  This `<text>` element denotes what the button says - you could also use a `<text translatable="true">` here and have it be translated instead
    

We really encourage you to write this yourself instead of simply copying it - the autocomplete in your IDE should make it a very fast process and will also make you discover many of the other components and options available. Once you're done with this, you can open the screen again and see that it looks exactly like the end result of the previous example! But wait, there's one thing missing - the button does not do anything when clicked.

Let's fix that by going back to our screen class' `build(...)` method. In here, you can query the button using the ID we just gave it. To do this, you call `childById(...)` on the root component. It is important to note here that IDs need not be unique within your hierarchy - this method simply returns the first matching component it comes across. For type safety reasons we also need to provide the type of component we're looking for, which, since we want the button, is `ButtonComponent.class`. After you have acquired the button this way, you can configure `onPress` like any other property:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-9-1) @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-9-2) protected void build(FlowLayout rootComponent) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-9-3)     rootComponent.childById(ButtonComponent.class, "the-button").onPress(button -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-9-4)         System.out.println("click"); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-9-5)     }); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#__codelineno-9-6) }`

After reloading your game, the button will work as expected.

What's next[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#whats-next "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Before jumping right in building UIs, we recommend checkout out the [Component Basics](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/component-basics/)
 and Layout Basics pages as they explain some more basic concepts you should be familiar with.

* * *

1.  The root component factory is quite simply a function which accepts the horizontal and vertical sizing and returns a matching component - don't worry too much about this right now. [↩](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#fnref:1 "Jump back to footnote 1 in the text")
    

* * *

# Utility Components - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/utility-components/#scroll-container)

Utility Components
==================

**Work-in-progress**

Besides the obvious essentials like buttons, labels and basic layouts, owo-ui also offers a range of utility components that solve problems commonly encountered during UI design.

### Scroll Container[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/utility-components/#scroll-container "Permanent link")

`<scroll direction="vertical|​horizontal">`  
`Containers.verticalScroll(...)` | `Containers.horizontalScroll(...)`

The scroll container is flexible solution to making anything scrollable. It's a parent component that accepts a single child and provides it infinite space on the scrollable axis. When scrolled, it relocates its children according to the current scroll offset instead of only shifting their rendering positions - it does not however cause any state updates to be emitted.

### Draggable Container[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/utility-components/#draggable-container "Permanent link")

`<drag>`  
`Containers.draggable(...)`

When you want a component to be movable on screen (just like an application window), you can use the draggable container. It wraps its single child and adds an extra bit of space (dubbed the "forehead") above, which can be grabbed with the mouse to move the entire component on screen.

### Collapsible Container[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/utility-components/#collapsible-container "Permanent link")

`<collapsible expanded="true|false">`  
`Containers.collapsible(...)`

The collapsible container is an extension of a flow layout that allows collapsible its children out of sight. It displays an arrow hinting at the fact it can be expanded as well as a title describing its content. Other than that, it behaves like a standard flow layout.

### Overlay Container[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/utility-components/#overlay-container "Permanent link")

`Containers.overlay(...)`

The overlay container does exactly what it sounds like - display its child as an overlay over its entire parent. This is primarily intended for dialog-like pop-ups, in which case you'd want to add the overlay as a child directly to the root component.

By default, the overlay closes when clicked outside the bounding box of its content - you can configure this behavior with `closeOnClick(...)`

### Dropdown Component[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/utility-components/#dropdown-component "Permanent link")

`<dropdown>`  
`Components.dropdown(...)`

The dropdown component is a generic dropdown pane as usually associated with context menus. It natively supports nesting and provides the static `openContextMenu(..)` utility function for the most common use-case.

Just like any other component, you add entries by calling the respective functions like `.divider()` and `.checkbox(...)`, which append minimal interactive components to the internal layout maintained by the dropdown.

* * *

Last update: 2023-01-29

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/utility-components/#)

---

# Button - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/button/#button)

Button[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/button/#button "Permanent link")

===============================================================================================

`<button>`  
`Components.button(...)`

The button component represents a clickable button. It can display text and respond to click events.

**Parameters:**

*   `text` (required): The text to display on the button.
*   `active`: Whether the button is active or not.
*   `renderer`: The button renderer to use for custom button styles.

**Example (Code-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/button/#__codelineno-0-1) Components.button(Text.literal("Click me!"), button -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/button/#__codelineno-0-2)     // Handle button click event [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/button/#__codelineno-0-3) })`

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/button/#__codelineno-1-1) <button> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/button/#__codelineno-1-2)     <text>Click me!</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/button/#__codelineno-1-3)     <active>true</active> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/button/#__codelineno-1-4) </button>`

* * *

Last update: 2024-03-22

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/button/#)

# owo-ui Components - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/#introduction)

owo-ui Components
=================

Work-in-progress

The owo-ui documentation is still being written and not quite complete yet. In places where an article here is still missing, you can always refer to the JavaDoc present throughout the library - it explains most things in detail

Introduction[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/#introduction "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

owo-ui provides a rich set of components that can be used to build interactive and customizable user interfaces. By leveraging these components and their various properties, you can create dynamic and visually appealing UIs using either the code-driven or data-driven approach.

For more detailed information on each component and their usage, please refer to the individual component documentation.

* * *

Last update: 2024-03-22

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/#)

# Collapsible Container - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#collapsible-container)

Collapsible Container[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#collapsible-container "Permanent link")

============================================================================================================================================

`<collapsible>`  
`Containers.collapsible(...)`

The collapsible container component allows you to create a collapsible section that can be expanded or collapsed. It supports a title text and various sizing and alignment options.

**Parameters:**

*   `expanded`: Whether the collapsible container is initially expanded or not.
*   `text`: The title text of the collapsible container.
*   `padding`: The padding around the child components.
*   `surface`: The background surface of the collapsible container.
*   `horizontal-alignment`: The horizontal alignment of the child components.
*   `vertical-alignment`: The vertical alignment of the child components.
*   `allow-overflow`: Whether to allow child components to overflow the bounds of the collapsible container.

**Example (Code-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-0-1) Containers.collapsible(Sizing.content(), Sizing.content(), Text.literal("Collapsible Section"), true) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-0-2)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Content"))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-0-3)     .padding(Insets.of(10)) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-0-4)     .surface(Surface.PANEL) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-0-5)     .horizontalAlignment(HorizontalAlignment.CENTER) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-0-6)     .verticalAlignment(VerticalAlignment.CENTER)`

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-1) <collapsible expanded="true"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-2)     <text>Collapsible Section</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-3)     <children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-4)         <label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-5)             <text>Content</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-6)         </label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-7)     </children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-8)     <padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-9)         <all>10</all> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-10)     </padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-11)     <surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-12)         <panel/> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-13)     </surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-14)     <horizontal-alignment>center</horizontal-alignment> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-15)     <vertical-alignment>center</vertical-alignment> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#__codelineno-1-16) </collapsible>`

* * *

Last update: 2025-02-03

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/collapsible-container/#)

# Checkbox - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/checkbox/#checkbox)

Checkbox[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/checkbox/#checkbox "Permanent link")

=====================================================================================================

`<checkbox>`  
`Components.checkbox(...)`

The checkbox component represents a toggleable checkbox. It can display text alongside the checkbox.

**Parameters:**

*   `text`: The text to display next to the checkbox.
*   `checked`: Whether the checkbox is checked or not.
*   `active`: Whether the checkbox is active or not.

**Example (Code-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/checkbox/#__codelineno-0-1) Components.checkbox(Text.literal("Option")) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/checkbox/#__codelineno-0-2)     .checked(false)`

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/checkbox/#__codelineno-1-1) <checkbox> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/checkbox/#__codelineno-1-2)     <text>Option</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/checkbox/#__codelineno-1-3)     <checked>true</checked> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/checkbox/#__codelineno-1-4)     <active>false</active> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/checkbox/#__codelineno-1-5) </checkbox>`

* * *

Last update: 2025-02-03

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/checkbox/#)

# Flow Layout - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#flow-layout)

Flow Layout[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#flow-layout "Permanent link")

==============================================================================================================

`<flow-layout>`  
`Containers.verticalFlow(...)` | `Containers.horizontalFlow(...)`

The flow layout component arranges its children in a vertical or horizontal flow. It supports various alignment and sizing options.

**Parameters:**

*   `direction` (required): The direction of the flow layout (`vertical`, `horizontal`, or `ltr-text-flow`).
*   `gap`: The gap between child components in pixels.
*   `padding`: The padding around the child components.
*   `surface`: The background surface of the flow layout.
*   `horizontal-alignment`: The horizontal alignment of the child components.
*   `vertical-alignment`: The vertical alignment of the child components.
*   `allow-overflow`: Whether to allow child components to overflow the bounds of the flow layout.

**Example (Code-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-0-1) Containers.verticalFlow(Sizing.fill(100), Sizing.content()) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-0-2)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Item 1"))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-0-3)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Item 2"))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-0-4)     .gap(10) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-0-5)     .padding(Insets.of(20)) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-0-6)     .surface(Surface.PANEL) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-0-7)     .horizontalAlignment(HorizontalAlignment.CENTER) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-0-8)     .verticalAlignment(VerticalAlignment.CENTER)`

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-1) <flow-layout direction="vertical"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-2)     <children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-3)         <label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-4)             <text>Item 1</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-5)         </label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-6)         <label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-7)             <text>Item 2</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-8)         </label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-9)     </children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-10)     <gap>10</gap> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-11)     <padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-12)         <all>20</all> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-13)     </padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-14)     <surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-15)         <panel/> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-16)     </surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-17)     <horizontal-alignment>center</horizontal-alignment> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-18)     <vertical-alignment>center</vertical-alignment> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/flow-layout/#__codelineno-1-19) </flow-layout>`

* * *

Last update: 2024-03-22
