# Dropdown - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#dropdown)

Dropdown[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#dropdown "Permanent link")

=====================================================================================================

`<dropdown>`  
`Components.dropdown(...)`

The dropdown component creates a dropdown menu with various entries such as buttons, checkboxes, and nested dropdowns. It supports customizable entries and various sizing and alignment options.

**Parameters:**

*   `close-when-not-hovered`: Whether to automatically close the dropdown when the mouse is not hovering over it.
*   `entries`: The entries of the dropdown menu.
*   `padding`: The padding around the dropdown entries.
*   `surface`: The background surface of the dropdown.
*   `horizontal-alignment`: The horizontal alignment of the dropdown entries.
*   `vertical-alignment`: The vertical alignment of the dropdown entries.
*   `allow-overflow`: Whether to allow the dropdown entries to overflow the bounds of the dropdown.

**Example (Code-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-1) Components.dropdown(Sizing.content()) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-2)     .button(Text.literal("Option 1"), button -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-3)         // Handle button click event [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-4)     }) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-5)     .checkbox(Text.literal("Option 2"), false, ignored -> {}) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-6)     .nested(Text.literal("Submenu"), Sizing.content(), submenu -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-7)         submenu.button(Text.literal("Submenu Option"), button -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-8)             // Handle submenu button click event [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-9)         }); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-10)     }) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-11)     .closeWhenNotHovered(false) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-12)     .padding(Insets.of(5)) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-0-13)     .surface(Surface.TOOLTIP)`

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-1) <dropdown> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-2)     <close-when-not-hovered>false</close-when-not-hovered> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-3)     <entries> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-4)         <button> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-5)             <text>Option 1</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-6)         </button> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-7)         <checkbox> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-8)             <text>Option 2</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-9)             <checked>false</checked> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-10)         </checkbox> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-11)         <nested name="Submenu" translate="false"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-12)             <button> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-13)                 <text>Submenu Option</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-14)             </button> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-15)         </nested> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-16)     </entries> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-17)     <padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-18)         <all>5</all> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-19)     </padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-20)     <surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-21)         <tooltip/> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-22)     </surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/dropdown/#__codelineno-1-23) </dropdown>`

# Label - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#label)

Label[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#label "Permanent link")

============================================================================================

`<label>`  
`Components.label(...)`

The label component is used to display text on the screen. It supports various text alignment options and can be styled with different colors and shadow effects.

**Parameters:**

*   `text` (required): The text to display in the label.
*   `max-width`: The maximum width of the label in pixels.
*   `line-height`: The line height of the text in pixels.
*   `color`: The color of the text.
*   `shadow`: Whether to apply a shadow effect to the text.
*   `vertical-text-alignment`: The vertical alignment of the text within the label.
*   `horizontal-text-alignment`: The horizontal alignment of the text within the label.

**Example (Code-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-0-1) Components.label(Text.literal("Hello, World!")) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-0-2)     .color(Color.ofRgb(0xffffff)) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-0-3)     .shadow(true) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-0-4)     .horizontalTextAlignment(HorizontalAlignment.CENTER) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-0-5)     .verticalTextAlignment(VerticalAlignment.CENTER)`

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-1-1) <label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-1-2)     <text>Hello, World!</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-1-3)     <color>#ffffff</color> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-1-4)     <shadow>true</shadow> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-1-5)     <horizontal-text-alignment>center</horizontal-text-alignment> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-1-6)     <vertical-text-alignment>center</vertical-text-alignment> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#__codelineno-1-7) </label>`

* * *

Last update: 2025-02-03

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/label/#)

# Slider - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#slider)

Slider[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#slider "Permanent link")

===============================================================================================

`<slider>`  
`Components.slider(...)`

The slider component represents a draggable slider for selecting a value within a range.

**Parameters:**

*   `text`: The text to display alongside the slider.
*   `value`: The current value of the slider.
*   `active`: Whether the slider is active or not.

**Example (Code-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-0-1) Components.slider(Sizing.fill(50)) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-0-2)     .message(s -> Text.literal("Volume")) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-0-3)     .active(true)`

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-1-1) <slider> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-1-2)     <text>Volume</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-1-3)     <value>0.5</value> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-1-4)     <active>true</active> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-1-5)     <sizing> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-1-6)         <horizontal method="fill">20</horizontal> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-1-7)         <vertical method="fixed">10</vertical> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-1-8)     </sizing> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/slider/#__codelineno-1-9) </slider>`

* * *

Last update: 2025-04-13

# Grid Layout - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#grid-layout)

Grid Layout[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#grid-layout "Permanent link")

==============================================================================================================

`<grid-layout>`  
`Containers.grid(...)`

The grid layout component arranges its children in a grid with a specified number of rows and columns. It supports various alignment and sizing options.

**Parameters:**

*   `rows` (required): The number of rows in the grid.
*   `columns` (required): The number of columns in the grid.
*   `padding`: The padding around the child components.
*   `surface`: The background surface of the grid layout.
*   `horizontal-alignment`: The horizontal alignment of the child components within each cell.
*   `vertical-alignment`: The vertical alignment of the child components within each cell.
*   `allow-overflow`: Whether to allow child components to overflow the bounds of the grid layout.

**Example (Code-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-0-1) Containers.grid(Sizing.content(), Sizing.content(), 2, 2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-0-2)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Cell 1")), 0, 0) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-0-3)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Cell 2")), 0, 1) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-0-4)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Cell 3")), 1, 0) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-0-5)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Cell 4")), 1, 1) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-0-6)     .padding(Insets.of(10)) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-0-7)     .surface(Surface.PANEL) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-0-8)     .horizontalAlignment(HorizontalAlignment.CENTER) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-0-9)     .verticalAlignment(VerticalAlignment.CENTER)`

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-1) <grid-layout rows="2" columns="2"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-2)     <children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-3)         <label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-4)             <text>Cell 1</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-5)         </label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-6)         <label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-7)             <text>Cell 2</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-8)         </label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-9)         <label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-10)             <text>Cell 3</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-11)         </label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-12)         <label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-13)             <text>Cell 4</text> </children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-16)     <padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-17)         <all>10</all> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-18)     </padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-19)     <surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-20)         <panel/> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-21)     </surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/grid-layout/#__codelineno-1-22) # Templates - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#template-basics)

Templates
=========

Template Basics[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#template-basics "Permanent link")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

`<template>`

The `template` tag allows you to define reusable components that can be inserted into your UI at different places. Templates are defined within the `templates` section of your owo-ui XML file and can be expanded and added to your UI using the `expandTemplate` method.

**Parameters:**

*   `name` (required): The name of the template, which is used to reference it when expanding the template.

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-1) <owo-ui xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-2)         xsi:noNamespaceSchemaLocation="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wisp-forest/owo-lib/1.20/owo-ui.xsd"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-3)     <components> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-4)         <!-- Your main UI components go here --> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-5)     </components> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-6)     <templates> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-7)         <template name="my-template"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-8)             <flow-layout direction="vertical"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-9)                 <children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-10)                     <label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-11)                         <text>My Text</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-12)                     </label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-13)                     <button id="the-click-me-button"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-14)                         <text>Click me!</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-15)                     </button> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-16)                 </children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-17)             </flow-layout> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-18)         </template> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-19)     </templates> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-0-20) </owo-ui>`

To use the template in your UI, you need to expand it using the `expandTemplate` method within your screen's `init` method. Here's an example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-1) public class Example extends BaseUIModelScreen<FlowLayout> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-2)     public Example() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-3)         super(FlowLayout.class, new Identifier("your-namespace-here", "your-ui-file-path-here")); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-4)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-5) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-6)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-7)     protected void build(FlowLayout rootComponent) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-8)         // Your regular code [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-9)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-10) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-11)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-12)     protected void init() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-13)         super.init(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-14) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-15)         if (this.uiAdapter == null) return; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-16) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-17)         this.uiAdapter.rootComponent.child( [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-18)             this.model.expandTemplate( [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-19)                 FlowLayout.class, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-20)                 "my-template@examples:example_ui", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-21)                 Map.of() [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-22)             ).childById(ButtonComponent.class, "the-click-me-button") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-23)             .configure(component -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-24)                 System.out.println("Button clicked!"); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-25)             }) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-26)         ); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-27)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-1-28) }`

In the `init` method, the `expandTemplate` method is called with the template name (`my-template@examples:example_ui`) and an empty map (`Map.of()`). This expands the template and adds the resulting components to the root component.

After expanding the template, you can access its child components using the `childById` method. In this example, the button component with the ID `the-click-me-button` is retrieved, and a click event handler is configured to print "Button clicked!" when the button is clicked.

Note that accessing components from a template should be done in the `init` method rather than the `build` method because the template components are not available during the build phase.

Value Replacement in Templates[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#value-replacement-in-templates "Permanent link")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Templates in owo-ui support value replacement, allowing you to customize the content of the template components when expanding them. You can define placeholders in your template using double curly braces (`{{placeholder}}`) and replace them with actual values when expanding the template.

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-1) <owo-ui xmlns:xsi="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema-instance" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-2)         xsi:noNamespaceSchemaLocation="https://raw.githubusercontent.com/wisp-forest/owo-lib/1.20/owo-ui.xsd"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-3)     <components> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-4)         <!-- Your main UI components go here --> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-5)     </components> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-6)     <templates> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-7)         <template name="my-template"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-8)             <flow-layout direction="vertical"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-9)                 <children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-10)                     <label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-11)                         <text>{{custom-text}}</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-12)                     </label> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-13)                     <button id="the-click-me-button"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-14)                         <text>Click me!</text> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-15)                     </button> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-16)                 </children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-17)             </flow-layout> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-18)         </template> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-19)     </templates> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-2-20) </owo-ui>`

In the above example, the label's text is defined as `{{custom-text}}`, which serves as a placeholder that can be replaced with actual text when the template is expanded.

To replace the placeholder values when expanding the template, you need to provide a map of key-value pairs to the `expandTemplate` method. The keys in the map should match the placeholder names, and the corresponding values will be used to replace the placeholders.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-1) @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-2) protected void init() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-3)     super.init(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-5)     if (this.uiAdapter == null) return; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-7)     this.uiAdapter.rootComponent.child( [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-8)         this.model.expandTemplate( [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-9)             FlowLayout.class, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-10)             "my-template@examples:example_ui", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-11)             Map.of("custom-text", "Hello, World!") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-12)         ) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-13)     ); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/templates/#__codelineno-3-14) }`

In the above example, the `expandTemplate` method is called with a map (`Map.of("custom-text", "Hello, World!")`). This replaces the `{{custom-text}}` placeholder in the template with the value "Hello, World!".

By using value replacement in templates, you can create more flexible and reusable components that can be customized based on the specific needs of your UI.

* * *

Last update: 2024-03-22

# Scroll Container - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#scroll-container)

Scroll Container[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#scroll-container "Permanent link")

=============================================================================================================================

`<scroll>`  
`Containers.verticalScroll(...)` | `Containers.horizontalScroll(...)`

The scroll container component creates a scrollable area for its child components. It supports vertical and horizontal scrolling, customizable scrollbars, and various sizing and alignment options.

**Parameters:**

*   `direction` (required): The direction of the scroll container (`vertical` or `horizontal`).
*   `scrollbar-thiccness`: The thickness of the scrollbar in pixels.
*   `fixed-scrollbar-length`: The fixed length of the scrollbar in pixels.
*   `scrollbar-color`: The color of the scrollbar.
*   `scrollbar`: The scrollbar renderer to use for custom scrollbar styles.
*   `padding`: The padding around the child components.
*   `surface`: The background surface of the scroll container.
*   `horizontal-alignment`: The horizontal alignment of the child components.
*   `vertical-alignment`: The vertical alignment of the child components.
*   `allow-overflow`: Whether to allow child components to overflow the bounds of the scroll container.

**Example (Code-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-1) Containers.verticalScroll(Sizing.content(), Sizing.fill(15), Containers.verticalFlow(Sizing.content(), Sizing.content()) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-2)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Item 1"))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-3)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Item 2"))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-4)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Item 2.1"))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-5)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Item 2.2"))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-6)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Item 2.3"))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-7)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Item 2.4"))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-8)     .child(Components.label(Text.literal("Item 3")))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-9)     .scrollbarThiccness(4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-10)     .scrollbar(ScrollContainer.Scrollbar.vanilla()) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-11)     .padding(Insets.of(10)) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-0-12)     .surface(Surface.PANEL)`

**Example (Data-driven):**

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-1-1) <scroll direction="vertical"> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-1-2)     <!-- Any component as child. We recommend a flow layout--> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/components/scroll-container/#__codelineno-1-3)     <flow-layout direction="vertical"> # Getting Started - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#creating-the-book-definition)

Getting Started
===============

**Work-in-progress**

When setting up documentation for a mod with Lavender, the very first step you need to take is creating the required file structure in your mod's resource pack. To begin, create a `lavender` directory in your mod's `assets`. To this, you _can_ now add the following subdirectories:

*   `books`  
    This is where all book definitions go - for every book you want your mod to declare you place a single `.json` file in here, the format on which is outlined in the next section.
    
*   `entries/<book name>/`  
    This is where you place your entries, potentially further organized into subdirectories. The entry format is briefly described below, but to get the full details you might want to [check out the respective article](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/metadata-format/)
    .
    
*   `categories/<book name>/`  
    All category definitions belong in here. Categories are used to group entries together, and work in much the same way (except that they don't support multiple pages)
    
*   `structures`  
    Structure definitions offer an easy way to display the layout of a multi-block structure to the reader _and_ preview it in the world
    

For `entries` and `categories`, as you can see, you place the files in a second subdirectory which is named like your book definition. That is, if your book is defined in a file called `my_book.json`, its entries will go into `lavender/entries/my_book/`

Creating the Book Definition[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#creating-the-book-definition "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To make your first book, create its book definition (for this example we'll be making `my_book.json`) and give it the required content:

my\_book.json

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-0-1) {}`

Yes, that is in fact all that's required for a minimal book definition - you just need to tell Lavender _somehow_ that your book exists at all. Of course, there are some other properties you _can_ set, but none of them are mandatory:

| Property | Description |
| --- | --- |
| texture | This is used to decide which texture to use for the GUI of your book. There are some built into Lavender following the `lavender:textures/gui/<color>_book.png` template |
| display\_completion | If some or all entries of your book are locked behind advancements, you can set this to `true` to make the book display a completion bar on the main index page and separately for each category |
| dynamic\_book\_model | Lavender has a built-in book, the _dynamic book_, which uses NBT data to emulate any book currently loaded into the game. This is primarily of interest if you are a modpack developer and thus cannot register your own book item through Lavender's API. You can set this property to another item model's ID (e.g. `mymodpack:my_book_model` -> `assets/mymodpack/models/item/my_book_model.json`) to make the dynamic book use said model when it is emulating your book |
| dynamic\_book\_name | The name the _dynamic book_ should display when it is set to emulate your book. This property expects a [Minecraft text object](https://minecraft.wiki/w/Raw_JSON_text_format#Appending)<br> (which can also be just a plain string) |
| extend | Should you be adding content to another mod with a Lavender guidebook, you can set this property to extend the original mod's book with your own entries and categories. To read more on how this works, look at the [respective article](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/writing-extensions/) |

Adding Entries[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#adding-entries "Permanent link")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Now that we have our book defined, let's start by adding a first entry. To do this, since our book is called `my_book`, we add `my_first_entry.md` into `assets/mymod/lavender/entries/my_book/` and give it the following content:

my\_first\_entry.md

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-1) ```json [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-2) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-3)   "title": "My First Page", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-4)   "icon": "minecraft:quartz", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-5)   "associated_items": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-6)     "minecraft:nether_quartz_ore" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-7)   ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-8) } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-9) ``` [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-10) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-11) In here, we put some **markdown-formatted** content for our entry. Lavender  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-12) supports most of the *standard* Markdown formatting syntax with some  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-13) {green}minecraft-specific{} extensions, like this one for color [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-14) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-15) ;;;;; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-16) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-17) This above page-break syntax (;;;;;) starts the next page. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-1-18) <recipe;minecraft:furnace>`

At this point, you're ready to open your book for the first time! Go ahead and start the game (or, if it is already running, do a resource reload with F3+T) - Lavender will now have loaded your book and the first entry we just wrote. To get yourself a dynamic book for testing, run `/get-lavender-book mymod:my_book`. Then, after opening the book and selecting your entry, you'll be greeted by the following screen:

![example entry in in-game book](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/lavender/book-screen-annotated.png)

The reload button and you

The reload button helpfully outlined in the above figure is only visible while running in oωo's [debug mode](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/system-properties/#-dowodebug-truefalse)
 and, when pressed, instantly reloads all book content (this includes book definitions!) from disk without having to sit through an entire client resource reload.

With this, however, it is important to note that neither Gradle not IntelliJ provide your mod assets directly from the source and instead copy them to some temporary directory. Thus, to properly sync your changes to the running game, you need to either rebuild or directly invoke IntelliJ's "Reload changed classes" action, after which you can do a reload and see your changes in-game

Further, if you take out some Nether Quartz Ore and hover it while having the book you just made in your hotbar, you'll see that (just as declared) the entry is referenced in the item's tooltip: ![example entry tooltip](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/lavender/associated-entry-tooltip.png)

Adding Categories[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#adding-categories "Permanent link")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Now that we have made an entry (and it should hopefully be abundantly clear how to create more of them), let's move on to creating a category. Analogously to entries, categories must be placed in the `assets/mymod/lavender/categories/my_book/` directory of your mod's resource pack (specifically, we'll save it as `a_category.md`). The format for categories, as you can see below, is very similar to entries - only the frontmatter is slightly different:

a\_category.md

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-1) ```json [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-2) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-3)   "title": "A Category", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-4)   "icon": "minecraft:dirt" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-5) } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-6) ``` [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-8) Just like __entries__, categories fully support **markdown formatting**. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-9) Be careful when writing their descriptions however, as you only get a [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-2-10) single page to work with.`

Now, in order for your category to actually show in the book, at least one entry must be inside it. To this end, modify the frontmatter of the entry we made previously:

my\_first\_entry.md

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-1) ```json [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-2) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-3)   "title": "My First Page", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-4)   "icon": "minecraft:quartz", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-5)   "category": "mymod:a_category", // new boi here [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-6)   "associated_items": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-7)     "minecraft:nether_quartz_ore" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-8)   ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-9) } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-10) ``` [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-11) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#__codelineno-3-12) ...`

After making these changes, sync them to your game instance and press the reload button to see them in action! You'll also have noticed by now that Lavender can handle entries without a category (contrary to what you might be used to from Patchouli). This can be quite useful if you have an introductory entry that doesn't really belong anywhere else _or_ if your mod is just not complex enough to warrant multiple categories.

Finishing up[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#finishing-up "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To end of this introductory tutorial, we'll add a landing page entry to the book to replace the smiley face greeting you upon opening it thus far. Luckily, this is as easy as creating an entry _directly inside_ `assets/mymod/lavender/entries/my_book/` which is simply called `landing_page.md` - it will automatically get picked up and displayed

### Further reading[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#further-reading "Permanent link")

While this introduction should get you up to speed on writing basic documentation, there's a lot more that Lavender has to offer in terms of Markdown syntax and metadata. To read more about this, check out the following articles:

*   [Metadata Format](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/metadata-format/)
     holds information on all flags and other metadata you can put into the frontmatter of both entries and categories
*   [Markdown Syntax](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/)
     is a comprehensive reference of all syntax elements supported by Lavender's Markdown implementation
*   [Writing Extensions](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/writing-extensions/)
     outlines the process of extending another mod's book with your own entries and categories - very helpful when making an add-on for another mod

* * *

Last update: 2024-04-02

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/getting-started/#)

---

# Writing Extensions - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/writing-extensions/#defining-an-extension)

Writing Extensions
==================

**Work-in-progress**

If you are writing an add-on to another mod which uses Lavender, you might want to integrate the documentation for your additions into the mod's existing guidebook. In order to keep clean separation between the original mod's and your addon's resources, Lavender offers **extension books** for this purpose.

### Defining an extension[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/writing-extensions/#defining-an-extension "Permanent link")

To turn your book definition into an extension, simply set the `extend` property to the ID of the original mod's book. The ID of a book is derived from the namespace in which the files are located and the path of the book definition's `.json` file relative to the `lavender/books` directory (e.g. a book defined in `assets/other-mod/lavender/books/strange_book.json` gets the ID `other-mod:strange_book`).

Once you have this property set, you add entries and categories to your book like normal - except that they now get added to the book you are extending instead of creating a new one. Naturally, this also means that you have access to all the content (namely entries and categories) defined in the original book and you can thus refer to said content in internal links.

* * *

Last update: 2023-07-07

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/writing-extensions/#)

---

# Metadata Format - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/metadata-format/#entries)

Metadata Format
===============

**Work-in-progress**

All properties marked in green are required

Entries[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/metadata-format/#entries "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The following properties are all applicable to entries - that is, you can declare them in the frontmatter:

| Property | Description |
| --- | --- |
| title | The title of this entry, to be displayed in the entry index and at top of the first page |
| icon | An item to use as this entry's icon in the index (optionally including NBT) |
| icon\_sprite | The identifier of a GUI sprite to use as this category's icon |
| category | The ID (relative to `.../entries/<book id>/`) of a category in which this entry should appear |
| associated\_items | A list of item (with optional NBT) which should link to this entry in their tooltip and, if the respective item is a block item, when looking at said block while holding the book |
| required\_advancements | A list of advancement IDs which the player must have completed before they can view this entry. If `display_completion` is `true` in the book definition, a progress bar will indicate to the player how many entries they have unlocked/left to go |
| secret | If this entry is locked due to a missing advancement, don't show it to the player at all instead of simply displaying it as locked |
| ordinal | A sorting index for this entry, displayed in ascending order. Entries with no ordinal are displayed last |

Categories[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/metadata-format/#categories "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The following properties are all applicable to categories:

| Property | Description |
| --- | --- |
| title | The title of this category, to be displayed at the top of its landing page |
| icon | An item to use as this category's icon in the index (optionally including NBT) |
| icon\_sprite | The identifier of a GUI sprite to use as this category's icon |
| secret | If all entries in this category are currently locked or invisible to the player, don't show it all instead of simply displaying it as locked |
| ordinal | A sorting index for this category, displayed in ascending order. Categories with no ordinal are displayed last |

* * *

Last update: 2024-03-06

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/metadata-format/#)

---

# scatter upload - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#scatter-upload)

`scatter upload`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#scatter-upload "Permanent link")

=======================================================================================================

The core command of scatter. Used to initiate the upload process. General syntax: `scatter upload <mod id> [version]` where `version` is optional

### Options[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#options "Permanent link")

#### `-o, --override-game-versions`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#-o-override-game-versions "Permanent link")

Do not use the configured Minecraft versions. Instead, a prompt is shown into which you can enter the appropriate versions.

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-0-1) → scatter upload <mod id> -o [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-0-2) ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-0-3) Comma-separated game versions: 1.17,1.17.1,1.17.2 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-0-4) ...`

* * *

#### `-f, --read-as-file`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#-f-read-as-file "Permanent link")

Always interpret the `[version]` argument as a file location. This is used to disable the artifact selection prompt and prevents scatter from making an attempt at interpreting said argument as a version. Instead, the given file will be uploaded without further checks.

Example: `scatter upload <mod id> mod.jar -f`

* * *

#### `-c, --confirm`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#-c-confirm "Permanent link")

Do not upload to each supported host automatically. Instead, you can choose for each host individually whether the artifact should be submitted.

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-1-1) → scatter upload <mod id> -c [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-1-2) ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-1-3) Upload to Modrinth? [Y/n] n [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-1-4) Upload to CurseForge? [Y/n] n [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-1-5) Upload to GitHub? [Y/n] n [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-1-6) ...`

* * *

#### `-r, --confirm-relations`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#-r-confirm-relations "Permanent link")

Do not declare each dependency automatically. Instead, you can choose individually for each dependency whether it should be declared.

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-2-1) → scatter upload <mod id> -r [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-2-2) ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-2-3) Declare dependency '<dependency id>'? [Y/n] n [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#__codelineno-2-4) ...`

* * *

#### `-l <mode>, --changelog-mode <mode>`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#-l-mode-changelog-mode-mode "Permanent link")

Do not use the default changelog mode. Instead, use either `editor`, `file` or `prompt`.

Example: `scatter upload <mod id> -l file`

* * *

Last update: 2022-10-04

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/upload/#)

---

# scatter edit - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/edit/#scatter-edit-mod)

`scatter edit <mod>`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/edit/#scatter-edit-mod "Permanent link")

===========================================================================================================

Edit a mod's entry in the database. This command launches an interactive session in which you can make edits without committing to any changes - type `save` to commit them or `done` to save and exit.

### Commands[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/edit/#commands "Permanent link")

#### `set <property> <value>`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/edit/#set-property-value "Permanent link")

Update a single property of the mod being edited. Available properties are:

| Property | Description |
| --- | --- |
| name | The display name of the mod |
| id  | The ID used to reference the mod in the database - changing this will forcefully save changes and exit |
| modloaders | The modloaders the mod should be marked compatible with. Accepts multiple, comma separated values |
| artifact\_directory | The directory where scatter searches for artifacts to upload |
| filename\_pattern | A filename pattern by which to filter when searching the artifact directory |
| changelog\_location | The location of a file from which to read the changelog when uploading a new version |
| version\_name\_pattern | The pattern by which to generate the name of versions when uploading, defaults to `[{game_version}] {mod_name} - {version}` |

#### `depmod <subcommand> <argument>`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/edit/#depmod-subcommand-argument "Permanent link")

Manage the dependencies of the mod being edited. There are two possible subcommands:

*   `depmod add <slug> <type>`  
    Add the mod with the specified slug to the dependencies, using the given type. This type must be one of `optional`, `required` and `embedded`
    
*   `depmod remove <slug>`  
    Remove the mod with the specified slug from the dependencies
    

* * *

Last update: 2022-11-12

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/edit/#)

---

# Structures - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#creating-a-structure-definition)

Structures
==========

Many mods involve multiblock structures of some kind, which can be hard if not nigh impossible to describe using text alone. It is almost always preferable to simply give the player a direct preview of what the structure looks like when fully built.

For this purpose, Lavender (much like Patchouli) offers structure preview & verification. The player can preview your structures in your book _and_ right in the world - layer by layer if necessary.

Creating a structure definition[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#creating-a-structure-definition "Permanent link")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In this tutorial, we'll be creating the structure definition for the well you see in this screenshot: ![a stone-brick well in minecraft](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/lavender/well-prebuilt.png)

To get started, create a JSON file in `assets/mymod/lavender/structures` - we'll call it `well.json`, for obvious reasons. Then, create the two base elements of a structure's definition. If you've worked with the JSON representation of shaped recipes before, this might look familiar:

*   `keys`, object  
    The keys object is a mapping from single-character keys to the block(s) they represent. The value associated with each key must be a stringified block state - the kind of input the `/setblock` command expects.
*   `layers`, array of arrays  
    Each inner array of the `layers` array describes a single layer of your structure, from the bottom up. Each layer in turn contains a string, where each character represents a block through the mappings defined in `keys`

Let's start by adding all of the keys required for the well:

well.json

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-2)   "keys": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-3)     "c": "minecraft:chiseled_stone_bricks", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-4)     "s": "minecraft:stone_brick_stairs[facing=north]", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-5)     "u": "minecraft:stone_brick_stairs[facing=south]", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-6)     "e": "minecraft:stone_brick_stairs[facing=east]", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-7)     "t": "minecraft:stone_brick_stairs[facing=west]", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-8)     "l": "minecraft:smooth_stone_slab", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-9)     "b": "minecraft:stone_bricks", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-10)     "w": "minecraft:stone_brick_wall", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-11)     "a": "minecraft:lantern" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-12)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-13)   "layers": [] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-0-14) }`

You'll notice that we added the Stone Brick Stairs four times, each with a different facing - this also nicely demonstrates how to use block state properties.

Now, let's get to defining the first layer of our structure. Let's take a look at just the first layer:

![first layer of well structure, isolated](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/lavender/well-first-layer.png)

To turn it into a layer, we simply go row-by-row, adding a new string to the layer's array for each. Remembering that the key for Stone Bricks is `b` and Chiseled Stone Bricks are `c`, we end up with this layer definition:

well.json

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-2)   "keys": { ... }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-3)   "layers": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-4)     [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-5)       "bbbbb", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-6)       "bcbcb", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-7)       "bbbbb", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-8)       "bcbcb", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-9)       "bbbbb" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-10)     ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-11)   ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-1-12) }`

Comparing this with the above snapshot of the layer in-game, the 1:1 correspondence between block layout and layer definition should be abundantly clear. We continue with the other layers in the same fashion, leaving us with a final structure definition that looks like this:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-2)   "keys": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-3)     "c": "minecraft:chiseled_stone_bricks", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-4)     "s": "minecraft:stone_brick_stairs[facing=north]", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-5)     "u": "minecraft:stone_brick_stairs[facing=south]", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-6)     "e": "minecraft:stone_brick_stairs[facing=east]", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-7)     "t": "minecraft:stone_brick_stairs[facing=west]", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-8)     "l": "minecraft:smooth_stone_slab", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-9)     "b": "minecraft:stone_bricks", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-10)     "w": "minecraft:stone_brick_wall", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-11)     "a": "minecraft:lantern" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-12)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-13)   "layers": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-14)     [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-15)       "bbbbb", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-16)       "bcbcb", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-17)       "bbbbb", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-18)       "bcbcb", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-19)       "bbbbb" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-20)     ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-21)     [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-22)       "culuc", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-23)       "e   t", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-24)       "l b l", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-25)       "e   t", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-26)       "cslsc" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-27)     ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-28)     [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-29)       "w   w", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-30)       "     ", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-31)       "  c  ", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-32)       "     ", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-33)       "w   w" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-34)     ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-35)     [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-36)       "a   a", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-37)       "     ", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-38)       "  b  ", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-39)       "     ", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-40)       "a   a" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-41)     ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-42)   ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#__codelineno-2-43) }`

You'll notice that where there's air (or, well, nothing) in our structure we put a space () - Lavender automatically interprets this to mean "anything goes" (including other blocks!). If you specifically want a space to be empty, use an underscore (`_`) instead.

Adding the structure to an entry[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#adding-the-structure-to-an-entry "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Just like the other game elements described in [Markdown Syntax](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#game-elements)
, a structure is inserted into an entry (or, if you need this for some reason, category) using the `<structure;"structure ID here">` syntax. Thus, to insert the structure we just defined, we use `<structure;mymod:well>`

![well preview inside a lavender book](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/lavender/well-book-preview.png)

Previewing in-game[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#previewing-in-game "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Once you have the structure successfully showing up in a book, simply clicking it suffices to place it into the game world. While the preview is following your view, you can scroll to rotate and then right-click to anchor it.

When the preview is placed, the progress-bar in the bottom left of your screen indicates progress towards completing the structure - it also turns red there is invalid block. Said blocks also get marked with a pulsating mining overlay to clearly indicate this information to the player.

![well preview in-game](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/lavender/well-world-preview-full.png) ![well preview in-game](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/lavender/well-world-preview-layer.png)

When your structure has multiple layers, like the well does, you can use the slider that appears next to the preview in the book to change which layer is displayed.

* * *

Last update: 2023-10-28

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/structures/#)

---

# Server Owners and Operators - Wisp Forest Docs

 

Server Owners and Operators
===========================

While gadget doesn't require a server mod for everything, the server mod is required for most privileged operations, including:

1.  Server-side inspection of entities (`gadget.inspect` or op level 4)
2.  Any modification of entity state via the inspector (`gadget.inspect` or op level 4)
3.  Changing item stack NBT, even in creative mode (`gadget.replaceStack` or op level 4)
4.  Requesting server datapack contents (`gadget.requestServerData` or op level 4)

Server owners should grant other players these permissions wisely, as some permissions (e.g. `gadget.inspect`) can allow players to break the server by editing important server fields. Generally, it's not recommended to put gadget on your production server unless you really need it.

* * *

Last update: 2023-08-31

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/for_server_admins/#)

---

# scatter config - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#scatter-config)

`scatter config`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#scatter-config "Permanent link")

=======================================================================================================

Edit scatter's configuration. Used for managing tokens as well as default game versions

### Options[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#options "Permanent link")

#### `--tokens`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#-tokens "Permanent link")

Configure the access token for a host. After selecting the host, you can safely enter the token - it will not be shown. When hitting enter, the token is saved, overriding one that's already present.

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-0-1) → scatter config --tokens [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-0-2) Platform: Modrinth CurseForge GitHub  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-0-3)                               ↑ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-0-4) Token (empty to remove):  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-0-5) info: Token for platform 'github' updated`

* * *

#### `--set-changelog-mode`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#-set-changelog-mode "Permanent link")

Change the preferred changelog mode

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-1-1) → scatter config --set-changelog-mode [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-1-2) Changelog mode: editor prompt file  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-1-3)                 ↑ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-1-4) info: Default changelog mode updated to 'editor'`

* * *

#### `--export`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#-export "Permanent link")

Export scatter's configuration and database as a bundle, without the saved tokens for security reasons. The bundle will be saved as `scatter-config-export.json`

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-2-1) → scatter config --export [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-2-2) info: Config exported to 'scatter_config_export.json'`

#### `--import <file>`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#-import-file "Permanent link")

Import a scatter configuration bundle from the given file. This will replace the current configuration and database, so be mindful when you use this.

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-3-1) → scatter config --import scatter_config_export.json [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-3-2) info: Config imported`

* * *

#### `--dump <type>`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#-dump-type "Permanent link")

Dump the given configuration file as well as its location on disk to the console, mainly useful for debugging purposes. Accepted types are `config`, `database` and `tokens` - be careful with the last one as it will dump all your tokens in plain text

Example:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-4-1) → scatter config --dump config [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-4-2) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-4-3)     "default_target_versions": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-4-4)         "1.18.2" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-4-5)     ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-4-6)     "default_changelog_mode": "editor" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-4-7) } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-4-8) info: Config file location: /home/<user>/.config/scatter/config.json`

* * *

#### `--default-versions`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#-default-versions "Permanent link")

Change the list of Minecraft versions with which all uploaded artifacts are automatically marked compatible

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-5-1) → scatter config --default-versions [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-5-2) info: Editing default versions. Prefix with '-' to remove a version, leave empty to exit [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-5-3) info: Use '-' to clear, '#' to display current default versions [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-5-4) info: Current default versions: [] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-5-5) Version: 1.18.2 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-5-6) info: Version '1.18.2' successfully added to default versions [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#__codelineno-5-7) Version:` 

* * *

Last update: 2022-10-04

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/scatter/config/#)

# Packet Dumping - Wisp Forest Docs

 

Packet Dumping
==============

gadget supports dumping all messages sent from and received by the client and viewing them via an in-game viewer.

![screenshot of the packet dump viewer](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/packet-dump-example.png)

This can greatly help with debugging all sorts of networking issues (barring TCP issues, of course) and makes it easier to see what was going on in a user's modpack without having to reproduce what was going on.

* * *

Last update: 2023-09-01

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/#)
