# Entity Inspector - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#sidebar)

Entity Inspector
================

The first (but sadly not most popular) feature of gadget is the entity inspector, with which you can inspect and edit (block)entities' server and client views. To inspect a (block)entity, press the `Inspect (default: I)` key while targeting it - all entities are included in the raycast, even ones that aren't collidable.

![entity inspector inspecting an chest](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/entity-inspector-example.png)

If you want to inspect yourself instead, just press `Inspect` while in any third person mode.

![entity inspector inspecting the player](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/entity-inspector-player-example.png)

The `S`/`C` button switches between the client and server views. If the server doesn't have gadget or the player doesn't have enough permissions, then only the client view is usable.

Server viewClient viewClient view on unsupported server

![S button hovered over with tooltip "Server view, click to switch to client"](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/entity-inspector-server-view.png)

![C button hovered over with tooltip "Client view, click to switch to server"](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/entity-inspector-client-view.png)

![C button hovered over with tooltip "Client view"](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/entity-inspector-client-view-no-switch.png)

The `E` (export) button can also be used to export the entire field dump as plain text or JSON.

Editing data[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#editing-data "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

While the entity inspector is mostly used for inspecting data, you can also use it for editing. Currently, only editing some primitives is supported (e.g. strings, integers, items), though support for more complex editing is planned.

To start editing a field, press the edit symbol next to the value. Pressing enter will finish the edit and apply changes, while escape will discard your edit. ![editing flySpeed field of player abilities](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/entity-inspector-editing.png)

Internals[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#internals "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The underlying widget of the field inspector (`FieldDataIsland`) is also embeddable into other UIs - it's even used to display packets in the [packet dump viewer](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/)
. This is one of the more complex subsystems of gadget, though, so we will start with the basics.

### Field objects[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#field-objects "Permanent link")

Every field value in gadget is represented by a `FieldObject`. There are 5 types:

1.  `primitive`  
    Describes any value that can be easily turned into a string and displayed with `PrettyPrinters.tryPrint`. Includes most basic standard library types, registry entries and `MinecraftServer`.
2.  `complex`  
    Used for all objects not described by the other field types. Represented as the value's type and its fields.
3.  `error`  
    Used if getting or converting the field's value resulted in an error.
4.  `nbt`  
    Used for `NbtCompound`s. Contains the tag inside it.
5.  `bytes`  
    Used for `byte[]`, `ByteBuffer` and `ByteBuf`. Shown as a hex dump.

The main class for gathering field data and getting field objects is `FieldObjects`, which has methods for getting class data and turning a value into a field object.

### `FieldDataHolder`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#fielddataholder "Permanent link")

`FieldDataHolder` is the abstract root of all field data managing classes. It supports reading in data asynchronously from a data source, dumping everything to plain text/JSON and using custom logic for field nodes. `FieldDataIsland` is just a subclass which provides owo-ui rendering capabilities. Additionally, the `DefaultFieldDataHolder` is provided if you don't want to extend anything and just want to deal with field data yourself.

Implementing a field data holder yourself is rather niche, but if you need to do it you mainly need to make a custom field node type and a way to make it from field data. Reference `FieldDataIsland` for anything else.

### `FieldDataSource`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#fielddatasource "Permanent link")

Field data holders are agnostic as to what place the field data is coming from. The data can be coming from an object on the same JVM (`LocalFieldDataSource`), or from the server (`RemoteFieldDataSource`, which is used for server entity inspection). Generally, you most likely want to just use the local field data source, but if you need some special processing or RPC, implementing `FieldDataSource` yourself is your best bet.

The contract of the interface makes getting the data of the root node synchronous (as it's immediately needed when making the data holder), so it's advised to send it with the initial packet if you're doing RPC. Furthermore, any RPC implementation should put timeouts on its futures (as otherwise the data holder will just wait indefinitely) and try to pass all errors to the caller.

### Embedding[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#embedding "Permanent link")

Embedding a basic field data island is incredibly simple:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#__codelineno-0-1) FieldDataIsland island = new FieldDataIsland( [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#__codelineno-0-2)     new LocalFieldDataSource(object, false), // (1) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#__codelineno-0-3)     false, // (2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#__codelineno-0-4)     false // (3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#__codelineno-0-5) ); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#__codelineno-0-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#__codelineno-0-7) out.child(island.mainContainer());`

1.  The second parameter to `LocalFieldDataSource` determines whether the view will allow changing the object.
2.  By default, complex field objects are shown as their type's full name. Setting this to `true` disables that.
3.  If you want to implement search for your data, enabling this will generate `SearchAnchorComponent` for every relevant field.

* * *

Last update: 2023-09-01

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/entity_inspector/#)

---

# Markdown Syntax - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#text-formatting)

Markdown Syntax
===============

**Work-in-progress**

Lavender offers a wide range of text-formatting syntax, most of which is just standard markdown, for adding emphasis and structure as well as entirely custom elements to your guidebook entries. This system is based on [lavender-md](https://github.com/wisp-forest/lavender-md)
, a highly flexible & extensible markdown processing engine, which also allows you to easily add custom syntax.

This article outlines the standard syntactical constructs supported by Lavender, from standard Markdown all the way to custom oωo-ui templates

Text Formatting[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#text-formatting "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Emphasis[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#emphasis "Permanent link")

Like in all standard Markdown renderers, you use

*   `*single asterisks*` for _italic text_
*   `**double asterisks**` for **bold text**
*   `***triple asterisks***` for **_bold and italic text_**

Lavender intentionally does not support any of the alternative characters usually implemented by other renderers in an effort to encourage consistency

Furthermore, like in Discord for example, you can use

*   `__double underscores__` for underlined text
*   `~~double tilde~~` for ~strike-through text~

### Color[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#color "Permanent link")

To add color to a span of text, you open with `{<color here>}` and close with `{}`. The `<color here>` part can be one of two things: either one of Minecrat's text colors (like `red`) or a 6 digit `#RRGGBB` hex color. Refer to the following examples:

*   `{red}some red{} text`  
    some red text
*   `{#F1C27B}a hex color with {light_purple}interspersed purple{} and{} back`  
    a hex color with interspersed purple and back

### Links[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#links "Permanent link")

Using standard Markdown syntax, wrap some text into `[square brackets](followed by a link in parantheses)` to create a [hyperlink](https://youtu.be/dQw4w9WgXcQ)
.

However, Lavender also offers specific syntax for linking to other entries or categories in the same book. To create an internal link, begin it with a caret `^` and follow with the ID of an entry or category (derived using the resource's namespace and path relative to their respective directory). Refer to these handy examples:

*   `[category link](^mymod:a_category)`  
    Links to `assets/mymod/lavender/categories/<book id>/a_category.md`
*   `[entry link](^mymod:basics/an_entry)`  
    Links to `assets/mymod/lavender/entries/<book id>/basics/an_entry.md`

Text Structuring[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#text-structuring "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Block Quotes[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#block-quotes "Permanent link")

Once again referring to standard Markdown, you prefix some lines of text with `>` to turn them into a quote. You can also repeat this symbol to increase the quote nesting depth. Refer to the following examples:

InputRendered

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-0-1) > block quote here [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-0-2) > [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-0-3) > very profound`

> block quote here
> 
> very profound

InputRendered

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-1-1) > quote level 1 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-1-2) >> now onto level 2 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-1-3) > and back onto 1`

> quote level 1
> 
> > now onto level 2
> 
> and back onto 1

### Horizontal Rules[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#horizontal-rules "Permanent link")

Continuing this trend, you can also insert a horizontal rule like this one

* * *

using `---` triple dashes. Unlike most other renderers, Lavender once again specifically does not support any alternative characters for this to encourage consistency

### Lists[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#lists "Permanent link")

Lavender supports both ordered & unordered lists which can contain any other Markdown. Like with other syntax elements that allow multple kinds of characters, you are required to use `-` dashes for unordered lists - like so:

InputRendered

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-2-1) - an element [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-2-2) - another one [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-2-3)     - and a nested one [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-2-4)         - deeper [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-2-5) - and back to base`

*   an element
*   another one
    *   and a nested one
        *   deeper
*   and back to base

To instead create an ordered list, simply replace the dashes with the item's index - like so:

InputRendered

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-3-1) 1. an element [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-3-2) 2. another one [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-3-3)     3. and a nested one [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-3-4)         4. deeper [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-3-5) 7. and back to base`

1.  an element
2.  another one
    1.  and a nested one
        1.  deeper
3.  and back to base

Do note that, unlike in this demonstration using MkDocs' markdown renderer, Lavender does not renumber your elements and instead uses the index you provide verbatim

### Page Breaks[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#page-breaks "Permanent link")

In order to prevent inconsistent results and confusing rules, Lavender makes no attempts to automatically break your entries into pages. Instead, you need to manually insert a page break, like this:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-4-1) ...page 1 content here... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-4-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-4-3) ;;;;; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-4-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-4-5) ...page 2 content here...`

Notice the two blank lines above and below the page break - they are part of this syntax and must not be omitted

Game Elements[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#game-elements "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### Keybinds[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#keybinds "Permanent link")

To insert a dynamically updating reference to a keybinding, use `<keybind;"translation key of binding here">` - like this:

`<keybind;key.attack>` renders as ![keybind tooltip example](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/lavender/keybind-tooltip.png)

To get the translation key of a given keybind, look it up in game's `options.txt` file. You'll notice that it saves the keybindings using a `key_` prefix - you need to drop this. The key in our example here is stored as `key_key.attack` in the file, yet we only use `key.attack`

### Translations[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#translations "Permanent link")

0.1.3

To insert a string translated using the game's translation system, wrap the key in `%{...}%`. For instance, `%{item.minecraft.diamond}%` would display the translated name of the diamond item in the client's active language.

### Entities, Items, Blocks and Recipes[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#entities-items-blocks-and-recipes "Permanent link")

To insert a preview of the mentioned game elements, you use the same syntax as for keybindings - like in these examples:

*   `<entity;minecraft:zombie>`  
    Insert a Zombie
    
*   `<entity;minecraft:zombie{IsBaby:1b}>`  
    Insert a Baby Zombie by providing the relevant NBT tag in addition to the entity ID
    
*   `<item;minecraft:diamond_shovel>`  
    Inserts a Diamond Shovel, with a proper functioning tooltip as well
    
*   `<item;minecraft:diamond_shovel{Enchantments:[{id: "minecraft:efficiency", lvl: 5}]}>`  
    Inserts a Diamond Shovel enchanted with Efficiency V by providing the relevant NBT tag in addition to the item ID
    
*   `<block;minecraft:furnace>`  
    Insert a Furnace
    
*   `<block;minecraft:furnace[lit=true]>`  
    Inserts a lit Furnace by providing the relevant block state properties. NBT for block entities is supported as well (you can use the `/setblock` command as reference for the syntax)
    

### Recipes[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#recipes "Permanent link")

To insert a dynamically updating recipe preview, use the familiar syntax for `recipe` and supply the recipe's ID - like this: `<recipe;minecraft:warped_fence_gate>`

![warped fence gate recipe preview](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/lavender/recipe-preview.png)

Do note that this preview is entirely dynamic, and if the recipe gets changed or replaced (even by one of an entirely separate type) it will still be accurate. By default, all Vanilla recipe types are supported - if you are a mod author you can add your own ones using Lavender's simple API. Specifically, take a look at `BookScreen.registerRecipeHandler`.

### Textures (Images)[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#textures-images "Permanent link")

Images in lavender-md are a bit of a special case, as they actually display textures and not arbitrary images loaded from the internet. The basic syntax is identical to standard markdown: `![<tooltip>](<texture resource ID>)`.

For example, to display the Fire Resistance icon, use the following: `![Fire Resistance](minecraft:textures/mob_effect/fire_resistance.png)`

As you'll notice, by default the texture is display with its actual size - however, this is not usually desireable when you need to display an image on your page. To make Lavender stretch the texture to the width of the page, append `,fit` after the resource ID.

As another example, to display the Furnace's GUI texture scaled to fit the page, use: `![Furnace](minecraft:textures/gui/container/furnace.png,fit)`

#### Adding your own textures[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#adding-your-own-textures "Permanent link")

For the presumably most common use-case, displaying your own images, you need to include said image as a texture resource in your mod's resource pack (that is, somewhere in `assets/mymod/textures`). Ideally, you make them 256x256 in size - we love our good ol' powers of two.

oωo-ui Templates[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#oo-ui-templates "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The most flexible way of creating custom components for you pages (without writing code, that is), is by using oωo-ui templates. You can read some more on how to create UI-models [here](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/ui/getting-started/#data-driven)
.

Once you have a UI model with your template in it, you can use the following syntax to insert it into Lavender markdown:

`<|template-name@ui-model-id|>`  
or, if your template takes parameters  
`<|template-name@ui-model-id|param1=value1,param2=value2|>`

If any of your template parameters contain a comma, you can escape it using `\`

owo-ui Models[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#owo-ui-models "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To directly embed some owo-ui model XML into your entry, create a code fence like this:

` [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-5-1) ```xml owo-ui [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-5-2)     ... model code here ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-5-3) ``` `

For instance, the following snippet would display a diamond on a dark panel background:

` [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-1) ```xml owo-ui [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-2) <stack-layout> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-3)     <children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-4)         <item> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-5)             <stack>minecraft:diamond</stack> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-6)             <set-tooltip-from-stack>true</set-tooltip-from-stack> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-7)         </item> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-8)     </children> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-9) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-10)     <padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-11)         <all>5</all> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-12)     </padding> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-13) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-14)     <surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-15)         <panel dark="true"/> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-16)     </surface> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-17) </stack-layout> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/lavender/markdown-syntax/#__codelineno-6-18) ``` `

![a rendered view of the above xml snippet](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/lavender/embedded-ui-model.png)

* * *

Last update: 2024-02-13

# Quick Start - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/quick_start/#recording-a-packet-dump)

Quick Start
===========

Recording a packet dump[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/quick_start/#recording-a-packet-dump "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you are already in game, then just pressing the `Dump Packets (default: K)` key will start dumping all traffic from that point. You can also just right click the specific entry in the Singleplayer/Multiplayer screen and then press `Join and start dumping packets` to join with the packet dumper enabled.

![context menu in singleplayer screen, with 'Join and start dumping packets' button highlighted](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/quick-start-world-context-menu.png)

If you want to stop and save the dump, you can just press the `Dump Packets` key again or leave the world - the toast will show the saved dump's file name. If you want to then manually inspect the dump file, it should be under `.minecraft/gadget/dumps`.

![toast saying 'Saved dump to 2023-09-01_16.47.40.gdump'](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/quick-start-saved-dump.png)

Opening a packet dump[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/quick_start/#opening-a-packet-dump "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A list of all dumps is in the gadget menu, which is accessible via the `G` button on the title/menu screen.

![gadget screen with a bunch of dumps listed](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/gadget-screen.png)

To open a packet dump, press the convenient `Open` button next to the file name to open the viewer. If you have a dump stored somewhere else, you can open a file picker with the `Open other dump` button.

Viewing a packet dump[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/quick_start/#viewing-a-packet-dump "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Warning

The UI doesn't work well on high GUI scales or low window sizes. GUI Scale 2 is recommended.

![dump viewer](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/quick-start-view-dump.png)

The dump viewer is conceptually a list of all packets in the dump together with some filters to not show everything at once. Most vanilla and supported modded packets are represented as the values of their fields, with unsupported packets just shown as a hex dump of their contents.

By default, the first 300 packets of the dump are shown. If you want to see later packets, the slider controls the point in time from which packets are shown. (Admittedly, this is a pretty short packet) ![dump viewer at the halfway point](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/quick-start-view-dump-slider.png)

If you want to filter by packet type, you can also use the search box, which searches by packet class and identifier. ![dump viewer with search box containing 'CustomPayload'](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/quick-start-view-dump-search.png)

* * *

Last update: 2023-09-01

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/quick_start/#)

# Defining new Forges though Data - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#where-do-i-define-it)

Defining new Forges though Data
===============================

Where do I define it?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#where-do-i-define-it "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When Alloy Forgery is loaded for the first time it generates a folder in the `.minecraft` directory, which is called `moddata`. Under the `moddata` folder you can create new forges, and override existing ones. An example would be overriding the deepslate forge. For this we would create enough folders so that we can go into `moddata/alloy_forgery/alloy_forges`, and create a new `deepslate_bricks_forge.json` file. This new file _will override_ the existing deepslate bricks forge, allowing us to change it.

For creating new forges simply create your own data folder. An example would be `moddata/custom_content/alloy_forges`, with a new `bedrock_forge.json` file inside.

Defining the forge[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#defining-the-forge "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

An example is provided below:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-2)   "material": "minecraft:deepslate_bricks", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-3)   "additional_materials": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-4)     "minecraft:deepslate_tiles", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-5)     "minecraft:polished_deepslate", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-6)     "minecraft:chiseled_deepslate" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-7)   ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-8)   "tier": 2, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-9)   "speed_multiplier": 1.5, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-10)   "fuel_capacity": 96000 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#__codelineno-0-11) }`

| Field | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `material` | Defines the block used for crafting the Forge Controller and the block the Forge is built from. |
| `additional_materials` | Defines extra materials the Forge structure can be built from. |
| `tier` | The tier of the Forge. Determines what recipes it can process. |
| `fuel_capacity` | How much fuel the Forge can hold before needing to be refueled. |
| `speed_multiplier` | A multiplier which decides how fast the Forge processes a recipe. Does not impact fuel consumption. |

* * *

Last update: 2024-05-23

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/defining-a-forge/#)

# NBT Inspector - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#editing)

NBT Inspector
=============

While direct field editing is adequate for entities and block entities, items only have NBT data, so the NBT inspector exists mainly to edit attached data to item stacks.

To inspect a stack, press the `Inspect (default: I)` key while you're hovering over it in a handled screen. As usual, the arrow button hides/shows the tree element. ![inspecting a chest item with 64 redstone blocks](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/nbt-inspector-example.png)

Editing[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#editing "Permanent link")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you [have permission to change item stacks](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/for_server_admins/)
, then the NBT inspector allows you to do a bunch of basic NBT modification. The edit button allows you to edit the value of the associated row, and the remove button just removes the entire entry from the tag.

To add something to a tag, press the add button next to the entry (or the add button in the sidebar if it's the root tag). If the type of entry is not already predetermined (e.g. you're in a compound), then you will be shown the type picker. After the type is chosen, then it's just a matter of picking the name (or index if it's a list) of the new element and the inital value. Pressing enter finalizes the added tag. ![type selector with all nbt element types rooted at the sidebar add button](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/nbt-inspector-type-selector.png) ![to-be-created tag with key 'test' and value 20 of type byte](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/nbt-inspector-adding-tag.png)

Embedding[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#embedding "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

While the NBT inspector is directly used for inspecting item stacks in gadget, it's also made to be embedded into other UIs or trees. In fact, the field inspector uses it to represent NBT values: ![nbt island under the ItemStack#nbt field in the field inspector](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/nbt-inspector-in-field-inspector.png)

The main widget here is `NbtDataIsland`, as it is responsible for displaying and updating the NBT tag. The constructor takes in the original NBT tag and a `Consumer<NbtCompound> reloader` that is used whenever the tag is changed by the user. To use it, just instantiate it and add it to your owo-ui flow layout:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-1) var island = new NbtDataIsland(tag, reloader); // (1) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-3) view.child(island); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-5) if (source.isMutable()) { // (2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-6)     var plusLabel = Components.label(Text.of("+")); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-8)     GuiUtil.semiButton(plusLabel, (mouseX, mouseY) -> [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-9)         island.typeSelector( [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-10)             (int) (plusLabel.x() + mouseX), [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-11)             (int) (plusLabel.y() + mouseY), [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-12)             type -> subContainer.child(new KeyAdderWidget(island, NbtPath.EMPTY, type, unused -> true))) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-13)     ); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-14) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-15)     header.child(plusLabel); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#__codelineno-0-16) }`

1.  If you want the tag to be immutable, just pass in `null` as the reloader.
2.  Right now, making a root add button for the island is kind of clunky, as it generally expects you to manage the whole process yourself. This will most likely change in the future.

* * *

Last update: 2023-09-01

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/nbt_inspector/#)

# Adjusting Accessory Equipablity - Wisp Forest Docs

 

Adjusting Accessory Equipablity
===============================

To control general equipability of items into slots it is required to make Slot Predicates. Accessories has three builtin predicates that can be used by both Modders and Datapackers alike with such being Item Tags, Data Component, and Attribute.

Modders can add custom predicates programmatically to allow for more control over what can be equipped if needed for new slots or existing slots. For such you can register a custom predicate using the `SlotPredicateRegistry#register` method for your custom `SlotBasedPredicate`.

Altering Existing Predicates

It is best to not restrict what can be equipped within the **Default** Slots or others due to the possibility of other Modders or Datapackers accessories from being able to be equipped with the given slots. Adding new predicates that allow for new items to be equipped should attempt to return `Tristate.DEFAULT` value when possible.

`accessories:tag``accessories:component``accessories:attribute`

By placing items within the slots corresponding Item [Tag](https://minecraft.wiki/w/Tag)
, you can allow for the given item to be equipped within the target slot. For example you if you want to add an item to the default `hat` slot, you need to make a Datapack and add the given item to the `accessories:hat` tag located within the folder structure like so: `data/accessories/tags/item/hat.json`

By adding the `"accessories:slot_validation"` [Data Component](https://minecraft.wiki/w/Data_component_format)
 to a given ItemStack you can adjust what slots a given item is valid for by adjusting the components `"valid_slots"` and `"invalid_slots"` as instructed within the info about the given [component](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/itemstack_components/#slot-validation)

It is **recommend** to use `"accessories:component"` instead of this for better control but by adding attributes linked to specific slots you can control what a given accessory item can be equipped within. Such can either be done within `"accessories:attributes"` Data Component or programmatically with the `AccessoryAttributeBuilder`.

* * *

Last update: 2024-12-19

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_accessories_to_slots/#)

---

# Recipe Adaptation - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/recipe-adaptation/#blast-furnace-adaptation)

Recipe Adaptation
=================

Since 2.1.0, Alloy Forgery added a system to adapt existing recipes to alloy forging recipes. Currently, only Blast Furnace recipes are adapted to work with the forge.

Developed alongside this adaptation system is the ability to create tags for Recipes with such following the same format as any other tag just being the tags should be placed within the `{your_namespace_here}/tags/recipes/` folder within your datapack.

Blast Furnace Adaptation[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/recipe-adaptation/#blast-furnace-adaptation "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

By default, Alloy Forgery attempts to adapt all Blast Furnace recipes to work within the Alloy Forge combined with giving an output increase when reaching tier 3 forge. This System can be controlled by two methods:

### Tags[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/recipe-adaptation/#tags "Permanent link")

Included are some tags that are used to adjust the behavior of the recipe adapter. One of these is a blacklist for recipes altogether (`alloy_forge:blacklisted_blasting_recipes`) which, for each recipe ID within it, prevents the corresponding recipe from being adapted into an Alloy Forge recipe.

You can also specifically blacklist a blasting recipe from gaining the increased output by putting it within the (`alloy_forge:blacklisted_increased_blasting_outputs`) recipe tag.

### Config[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/recipe-adaptation/#config "Permanent link")

More recent versions of Alloy Forgery include a config file which contains some more options on controlling blasting adaption, such outlined below:

| Option | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `allowHigherTierOutput` | Allows for the ability to toggle on or off the tier increase on **ALL** Blasting Recipes. |
| `allowBlastingFurnaceAdaption` | Allows for the ability to toggle on or off the blasting adaption for **ALL** Blasting Recipes. |
| `baseInputAmount` | Adjusts the required input amount for the adapted Blasting Recipe. Such functions as a multiplier for both the input and output meaning that with the default value of '2', the required amount needed to craft is '2' with an output of '2'. |
| `higherTierOutputIncrease` | Controls the amount of increased output that is gotten when using a tier 3 Alloy Forge if such tier output was not disabled. |

* * *

Last update: 2024-05-24

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/recipe-adaptation/#)

---

# Default Slots - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/defaulted_slots/#default-implementations)

Default Slots
=============

By default Accessories provides builtin slots for use by other modders to give a starting point of shared slots. This is done to prevent a flood of slots with alternatives of the same concept, which leads to a cluttered UI and confusing equipment management.

We recommend you to try and use the available slots starting out unless your Accessory item does not fit under the default slots. For that, we suggest you consider [making your own through data](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#data-pack-format)
 or by using the [Unique Slot API](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#unique-slot-api)
.

Default Implementations[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/defaulted_slots/#default-implementations "Permanent link")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Below is the current default implemented list of Slot Types provided:

| Name | Usage | Examples |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `charm` | Items equipped into a pocketed area of the entity's body | Magic Stuff |
| `hat` | Items equipped on top of the entity's head | Crowns or Hats |
| `face` | Items equipped over the entity's face i.e. a mask | Masks or Glasses |
| `cape` | Items equipped around the entity's neck and drape down their back | Cloaks or Shirts |
| `necklace` | Items equipped around the entity's neck and hang in the front of their body | Necklaces or Collar |
| `back` | Items equipped on the entity's back around the chest or around the arms on both side | Backpacks or Shields |
| `hand` | Items equipped on the entity's hands either covering them fully or partially | Gloves or Gauntlets |
| `ring` | Items equipped on the entity's fingers | Rings |
| `wrist` | Items equipped around the entity's wrist | Watches or Bracelets |
| `belt` | Items equipped around the entity's waist | Belt or Pouches |
| `anklet` | Items equipped around the entity's ankle | Anklets |
| `shoes` | Items equipped on the entity's feet | Shoes or Socks |

* * *

Last update: 2024-12-26

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/defaulted_slots/#)

---

# Creating and Modifying Slots - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#data-pack-format)

Creating and Modifying Slots
============================

If the information below is still leaving you with questions, you can look at each platform's test mod \[[Fabric](https://github.com/wisp-forest/accessories/tree/fa06f044f5c7486b26a8c0774f7ca3edbd256cad/fabric/src/testmod)\
, [Neoforge](https://github.com/wisp-forest/accessories/tree/fa06f044f5c7486b26a8c0774f7ca3edbd256cad/neoforge/src/testmod)\
\] for starting points. You can also ask questions within the [Discord](https://discord.gg/xrwHKktV2d)
 for more assistance.

Creating a slot within Accessories requires you follow the two options available to you:

*   Datapack Method: Allows for full ability to tweak Slot Properties and its bound Entities within `json` data files loaded on server start
*   Programmatic Method: More restrictive control over a given slot type via the Unique Slot API

Notice for Datapacks

When using the Datapack method its recommended that you design your mod with the ability to be adjusted by end users/other datapackers. This is because of Accessories base systems, which allow for items to be moved from one slot to another, removed from your slot, or even preventing an item from being equipped in any slot.

It may be your intention to provide some sense of balance, but this will lead to issues for Modpack makers, who usually want to balance around other mods.

Data Pack Format[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#data-pack-format "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To create your own slot type or adjust an existing slot, you will need to need to make a new `.json` file at the following location, `data/{replace_with_pack_namespace}/accessories/slot/`, **that is named as the slots name**.

**For Unique slots**: it is required that you have the namespace of the given slot within the folder structure as follows: `data/{replace_with_pack_namespace}/accessories/slot/{unqiue_slot_namespace_here}/`.

Below is an example of the `back` slot file located within Accessories [here](https://github.com/wisp-forest/accessories/blob/c41504c63f5c608e1e0ea249fae8b1a152c92f29/common/src/main/resources/data/accessories/accessories/slot/back.json)
:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-0-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-0-2)   "replace": false, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-0-3)   "amount": 1, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-0-4)   "operation": "set", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-0-5)   "order": 1000, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-0-6)   "icon": "accessories:gui/slot/back" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-0-7) }`

| Field Keys | Data Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `"order"` | Integer | The number which decides in what order the slot will appear inside the Accessories Screen. Lower numbers are placed first and higher numbers are placed last |
| `"amount"` | Integer | Used when calculating the base size of the given slot using the given operation's: `"set"`, `"add"`, or `"remove"` |
| `"operation"` | String | The specific operation used in combination with the specified `amount` |
| `"validators"` | String\[\] | The ResourceLocation's (`Identifier`) of all predicates to be used for the given slot |
| `"drop_rule"` | String | The specific rule used when attempting to drop the Accessories: `"default"`, `"keep"`, `"drop"`, `"destroy"` |
| `"icon"` | String | The resource location of the given slot icon in which is used to find the texture within the block atlas |

Icon Location

It is recommended that the location for the icon follows the `assets/{replace_with_pack_namespace}/gui/slot/` convention. This is because any textures here are put within the block atlas (to allow for ticking). If this is not followed, it is up to the developer to add the texture to the block atlas for rendering to work

To modify existing slots there are multiple methods to such:

*   Modify Amount: Create a file with the same **same path** and **same name** with adjustments to amount either though the `add` or `remove` operation type
*   Replace File: Create a file with the **same namespace**, **same path**, and **same name** that you then adjust with the `replace` field set to `true` which will replace
*   Replace Data (Requires Datapack Ordering): Move your datapack using some tool or method(Not included by default) that allows for the adjustment of ordering allowing for your slot file to apply after the inital one allowing you to modify aspects of such

Unique Slot API[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#unique-slot-api "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This API is the alternative method for creating a slot which comes with the benefits of being able to lock down various aspects of a slot like equipability, which Entity a slot is bound to, and prevents certain operations like resizing from occurring.

Note that unique slots will not show up in the main Accessory Screen. Wit this you get the freedom to implement your own custom screen/system using Accessories as your backend/API target to interact with inventory.

A breakdown of how such is to implement is below:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-1) public class UniqueSlotExample implements UniqueSlotHandling.RegistrationCallback  { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-2)     private static final ResourceLocation MAGIC_BALL_PREDICATE = ResourceLocation.fromNamespaceAndPath("example", "magic_ball"); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-4)     public static final UniqueSlotExample INSTANCE = new UniqueSlotExample(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-5) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-6)     private UniqueSlotExample(){ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-7)         SlotPredicateRegistry.registerPredicate(slotPredicate1, SlotBasedPredicate.ofItem(item -> item.equals(ExampleItems.MAGIC_BALL))); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-8)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-9) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-10)     private static SlotTypeReference MAGIC_BALL_REFERENCE; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-11) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-12)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-13)     public void registerSlots(UniqueSlotHandling.UniqueSlotBuilderFactory factory) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-14)         MAGIC_BALL_REFERENCE = factory.create(ResourceLocation.fromNamespaceAndPath("example", "magic_ball"), 1) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-15)                 .slotPredicates(MAGIC_BALL_PREDICATE) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-16)                 .validTypes(EntityType.PLAYER) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-17)                 .build(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-18)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-19) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-20)     @Nullable [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-21)     public static SlotTypeReference magicBallRef() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-22)         return MAGIC_BALL_REFERENCE; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-23)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-24) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-25)     // Call init method within your mods initializer to add the class to the main Unique Slot Handling event [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-26)     public static void init() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-27)         UniqueSlotHandling.EVENT.register(UniqueSlotTest.INSTANCE); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-28)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#__codelineno-1-29) }`

Slot Initialization

You must call the init function of the example class or register the event invoker yourself

The given factory object that is returned by the registered method invocation or implementing object allows you to get a `UniqueSlotBuilder` which has the following methods:

| Field Keys | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `slotPredicates(ResourceLocation... locations)` | Used to pass the desired Slot Predicates for this slot as none are set by default |
| `validTypes(EntityType<?>... types)` | Used to pass any entity types that should be bound with this slot |
| `strictMode(boolean value)` | Used to prevent any modifications to key data like the given slot predicates or what entity have this slot bound |
| `allowResizing(boolean value)` | Used to prevent adjustments to the slot amount either though datapack or attributes |
| `allowEquipFromUse(boolean value)` | Used to prevent any Accessory valid for this slot type from being quickly equipped from hand |
| `allowTooltipInfo(boolean value)` | Used to prevent any tooltip information about this slot from appearing within a given Accessories Tooltip |

* * *

Last update: 2024-12-26

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_types/#)

# Adding Recipes and Fuels - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#creating-a-recipe)

Creating a recipe[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#creating-a-recipe "Permanent link")

===================================================================================================================================

When creating an Alloy Forge recipe you want to use the `alloy_forgery:forging` type.  
The recipe can be placed anywhere under `data/<namespace>/recipes` in your data.  
Here is an example of a recipe:

copper\_ingots\_from\_ore.json

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-2)   "type": "alloy_forgery:forging", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-3)   "inputs": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-4)     { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-5)       "tag": "minecraft:copper_ores" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-6)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-7)   ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-8)   "output": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-9)     "item": "minecraft:copper_ingot", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-10)     "count": 3 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-11)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-12)   "overrides": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-13)     "2": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-14)       "item": "minecraft:copper_ingot", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-15)       "count": 4 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-16)     }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-17)     "3+": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-18)       "item": "minecraft:copper_ingot", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-19)       "count": 5 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-20)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-21)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-22)   "min_forge_tier": 1, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-23)   "fuel_per_tick": 5 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-0-24) }`

Input Format[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#input-format "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The inputs follow the Minecraft ingredient format (used by most other recipes) with such being the identifier of a given item tag (`"tag": ...`) or entry (`"item": ...`) and an additional `count` field used to give info about how much of such is required.

A single recipe can accept, at max, **10** different ingredient entries. Furthermore, we also support any of Fabric's custom Ingredients like its Custom NBT-based Ingredient.

Output Format[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#output-format "Permanent link")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

There currently exist two methods of returning an item as an output:

### Item[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#item "Permanent link")

Using the `item` field as the item's identifier combined with a `count` for control on the stack size of such returned item. Such is shown above as the first example.

### Tagged[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#tagged "Permanent link")

**_Supported as of version 2.0.16+_**

Using the `default` field supplied with the desired target tag will allow for whichever entries within such to be used as an output though due to tags random ordering, it's best to supply a `priority` array of outputs to chose from that are known to work out the gate if found.

Tag Output Selection

The `priority` array will be sequentially checked to see if the specified entry exists and if none are found, will default to using the tag to try and find any entry to use as an output.

lead\_ingots\_from\_raw\_ore.json

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-2)   "fabric:load_conditions": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-3)     { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-4)       "condition": "fabric:item_tags_populated", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-5)       "values": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-6)         "c:raw_lead_ores", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-7)         "c:lead_ingots" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-8)       ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-9)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-10)   ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-11)   "type": "alloy_forgery:forging", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-12)   "inputs": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-13)     { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-14)       "tag": "c:raw_lead_ores", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-15)       "count": 2 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-16)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-17)   ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-18)   "output": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-19)     "priority": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-20)       "techreborn:lead_ingot", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-21)       "indrev:lead_ingot", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-22)       "modern_industrialization:lead_ingot" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-23)     ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-24)     "default": "c:lead_ingots", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-25)     "count": 3 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-26)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-27)   "overrides": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-28)     "2+": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-29)       "count": 4 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-30)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-31)   }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-32)   "min_forge_tier": 1, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-33)   "fuel_per_tick": 5 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-1-34) }`

### Overrides[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#overrides "Permanent link")

Overrides allow changing the output item depending on the tier of the Forge. Accepted formatting:

| Examples | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `"2"` | The override applies only to tier 2. |
| `"3+"` | The override applies to tier 3, and anything above it. |
| `"2 to 5"` | The override only applies to the specified range of tiers, in this case from tier 2 to tier 5. |

### Minimum Forge Tier[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#minimum-forge-tier "Permanent link")

`min_forge_tier` field indicates the minimum tier required to use this recipe.

### Fuel Per Tick[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#fuel-per-tick "Permanent link")

`fuel_per_tick` field indicates the amount of fuel consumed by the Forge per tick. One bucket of lava is 24000 fuel.

Recipe Remainders[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#recipe-remainders "Permanent link")

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

**_Supported as of version 2.0.17+, requires owo-lib 0.8.0+_**

Due to Vanilla's very generic recipe remainders, you can use owo's [Recipe Specific Remainders](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/recipe-remainders/)
 instead, allowing for fully customizable recipe remainders, or use the built-in global remainder system loaded through the `data/<namespace>/forge_remainder` folder.

A example for global Alloy Forgery remainders is below:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-2)   "remainders": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-3)     // Count is supported [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-4)     "minecraft:iron_ore": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-5)       "item": "minecraft:cobblestone", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-6)       "count": 4 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-7)     }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-8) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-9)     // Turn copper in input to sand [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-10)     "minecraft:copper_ore": "minecraft:sand", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-11)   } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-2-12) }`

In the upper example you can declare a map of your item to an object.

The initial Item ID here is the input to be replaced. Supported settings:

| Field | Description |
| --- | --- |
| `item` | The ID of the returned item. |
| `count` | Custom stack counts (optional) |

In the lower example, the initial item (copper ore) is what is being checked for, and the second item (sand) is returned once the recipe completes.

Adding new fuels[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#adding-new-fuels "Permanent link")

=================================================================================================================================

Alloy Forgery loads fuel from a specific folder in data. The path is `data/<namespace>/alloy_forge_fuels`, and in here you put your fuel definition. A fuel file does not require a specific name, and can hold multiple different fuels. Currently, we only support items for fuels, tags are not accepted. An example is provided below:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-2)   "fuels": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-3)     { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-4)       "item": "minecraft:lava_bucket", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-5)       "return_item": "minecraft:bucket", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-6)       "fuel": 24000 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-7)     }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-8)     { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-9)       "item": "minecraft:coal", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-10)       "fuel": 1000 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-11)     }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-12)     { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-13)       "item": "minecraft:charcoal", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-14)       "fuel": 1000 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-15)     }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-16)     { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-17)       "item": "minecraft:blaze_rod", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-18)       "fuel": 2000 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-19)     }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-20)     { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-21)       "item": "minecraft:coal_block", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-22)       "fuel": 9000 [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-23)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-24)   ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#__codelineno-3-25) }`

The special field `return_item` is optional, and is intended for when you want to do something similar to returning an empty bucket after using a lava bucket with the forge.

* * *

Last update: 2024-05-24

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/alloy-forgery/adding-recipes-and-fuels/#)
