# FAQ (Frequently Asked Questions) - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#general)

FAQ (Frequently Asked Questions)
================================

General[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#general "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### Can I change what slot something is equipped to?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#can-i-change-what-slot-something-is-equipped-to "Permanent link")

In theory you can do this, as you are able to modify an Accessory to be equippable in any slot. Due to limitations on both Minecrafts internal slot system, and Accessories API, there is no guarantee that an Accessory will _function_ if you do so.

#### Is it possible to remove a slot altogether?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#is-it-possible-to-remove-a-slot-altogether "Permanent link")

Yes, although it is not recommended for either modders or datapackers to take such drastic action, since it can really mess with mods progression or functionality.

It is understandable from a modpacking perspective that you would want to do this (condensing slots, rebalancing the pack, etc.). Do note that some developers might **lock their Accessories to their own slots**, meaning that restricting/removing these could fully break those items (and by extension mods).

#### Do enchantments work with equipped Accessories?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#do-enchantments-work-with-equipped-accessories "Permanent link")

If the item is able to be enchanted with a given enchantment then it is possible for the such enchantment to work almost natively with the base equipment system found within Minecraft but some edge case may exists where the enchantment will not function properly if outside the scope of the API.

### Equipment[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#equipment "Permanent link")

#### Can I put modded items within an Accessory slot?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#can-i-put-modded-items-within-an-accessory-slot "Permanent link")

In most cases the given mod needs to have implicit support for Accessories before the Item will function properly. We suggest that you check with mod authors if you are unsure.

#### Can I put Totems within an Accessory slot?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#can-i-put-totems-within-an-accessory-slot "Permanent link")

In the latest Releases for 1.21.2 and above, Accessories has builtin support for Totems. By default this is disabled, but you can enable the feature in the config. For developers, there exists some API for handling certain aspects of Totem logic if needed for compatibility or custom behavior.

#### Can I put Gliders like Elytra within an Accessory slot?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#can-i-put-gliders-like-elytra-within-an-accessory-slot "Permanent link")

In the latest Releases for 1.21.2 and above, Accessories has builtin support for Gliders. It is disabled by default, but you can enable the feature in the config.

#### Can I put Banners in an Accessory slot?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#can-i-put-banners-in-an-accessory-slot "Permanent link")

In the latest releases for 1.21.2 and above, Accessories has builtin support for Banners, which is enabled by default. It allows you to equip them on your head!

### Support[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#support "Permanent link")

#### Is there commands for adjusting the players slot amount?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#is-there-commands-for-adjusting-the-players-slot-amount "Permanent link")

No. This is planned for the future, with full documentation about the commands within Accessories.

#### Is there support for mods that adjust entity models and do cool animations?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#is-there-support-for-mods-that-adjust-entity-models-and-do-cool-animations "Permanent link")

There is a desire to have mods like [Figura](https://modrinth.com/mod/figura)
 be supported with custom models but this requires a good deal of effort to do properly. This is planned for the future.

Currently support for [Entity Model Feature](https://modrinth.com/mod/entity-model-features)
 is provided by some compat code, which has fixed various issues found with other Accessories APIs like Trinkets or Curios.

### Compat Layers[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#compat-layers "Permanent link")

#### I tried using the Trinkets/Curios Compat layer and its crashing, what do I do?[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#i-tried-using-the-trinketscurios-compat-layer-and-its-crashing-what-do-i-do "Permanent link")

Make sure that both the compat layers and the Accessories version are up-to-date. This is important as the layers need to be updated frequently to adjust for any changes that may occur within Accessories.

Other issues may be that a mod may be using API that isn't implemented, or accessing non-public API provided by Trinkets and Curios.

It may be possible to implement/support missing API, but in some cases it might be easier if the mod itself adds direct support for Accessories.

#### How do I go around adjusting slot amounts for mods using Trinkets/Curios Compat layer[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#how-do-i-go-around-adjusting-slot-amounts-for-mods-using-trinketscurios-compat-layer "Permanent link")

For mods adding slots though Curios API it is easy. All you need to do is to adjust it through the Curious datapack method, or via the Accessories config.

Trinkets can be adjust either using a datapack or through the Accessories config. You might require to adjust the format of the slot identifier to something like `trinket_group_{slot_group_name_here}-{slot_name_here}` in order for it to work properly.

This is due to Trinkets API using groups as logical paths, meaning the name of the slot within Accessories requires the group name to be combined with the slot name to prevent issues.

Developer[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#developer "Permanent link")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

#### Differences between Accessories and other Accessory API's[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#differences-between-accessories-and-other-accessory-apis "Permanent link")

Some notable differences compared to the likes of Trinkets and Curios:

##### Mod Development[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#mod-development "Permanent link")

*   Full Multiloader support for both major platforms (**Fabric** and **Neoforge**)
*   Fully programmatic method for creating unique slots
*   Support for Nested Accessories (Accessories within Accessories)
*   Expansive support for ModelPart targeting, with support for EMF

##### Gameplay[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#gameplay "Permanent link")

*   Multiple different screen variants depending on the desired style of play
*   Full support for Data Driven Accessories
*   Supports Cosmetic Armor/Accessories out-of-the-box
*   Additional toggleable features for equipping Banners as Accessories (on your head!)
*   Additional toggleable features for equipping Totems or Gliders as Accessories

##### Performance[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#performance "Permanent link")

*   Implement caching to alleviate bottle necks with querying Accessory inventories

#### Reason behind using owo-lib in the development of Accessory[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#reason-behind-using-owo-lib-in-the-development-of-accessory "Permanent link")

The main reason behind using owo-lib is down to its useful API's that leads to the development of Accessories being unhindered when it comes to UI, serialization, networking, and configuration.

The library is used to its full extent, apart from some minor core features. I decided to use it to keep development time down and allow for quicker implementation of features instead of developing and maintaining all that API from scratch. All of this is done to create a better experience for players.

* * *

Last update: 2024-12-26

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/faq/#)

---

# Binding Slots to Entities - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#data-pack-format)

Binding Slots to Entities
=========================

It is required that each Slot created needs to be implicitly bound to the desired entity type. By default, the given implemented slots are bound to any entity type found within the `accessories:defaulted_targets` **EntityType** tag which currently includes the `Player` and `ArmorStand` type.

Data Pack Format[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#data-pack-format "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To bind a slot to a given **EntityType** you will need to create a `.json` file at the following location: `data/{replace_with_pack_namespace}/accessories/entity/`. This file will need to contain to required fields: `entities` and `slots`.

| Field Keys | Data Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `"entities"` | String\[\] | A list containing either specific resource locations of Entity Types or an Entity Type Tag (prefixed with a hashtag `#`) |
| `"slots"` | String\[\] | A list of all slot names to be available to the given entities |

The example below is what Accessories uses to bind the Builtin Slots to the defaulted entity targets:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-2)   "replace": false, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-3)   "entities": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-4)     "#accessories:defaulted_targets" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-5)   ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-6)   "slots": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-7)     "hat", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-8)     "face", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-9)     "necklace", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-10)     "cape", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-11)     "back", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-12)     "hand", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-13)     "ring", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-14)     "wrist", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-15)     "belt", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-16)     "anklet", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-17)     "shoes", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-18)     "charm" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-19)   ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#__codelineno-0-20) }`

* * *

Last update: 2024-12-25

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/binding_slots_to_entities/#)

# Creating Slot Groups - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#data-pack-format)

Creating Slot Groups
====================

Slot Groups are mainly a cosmetic system meant to wrap certain slots in specific parts the body as a way to better order specific sets of slots and act as an easy method to quickly move to such specific slots within the Accessories Screen.

Data Pack Format[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#data-pack-format "Permanent link")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

To create your own Slot group or adjust an existing group, you will need to need to make a new `.json` file at the following location, `data/{replace_with_pack_namespace}/accessories/group/`, **that is named as the groups name**. Below is a detailed example on the given format:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#__codelineno-0-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#__codelineno-0-2)   "replace": false, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#__codelineno-0-3)   "order": 120, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#__codelineno-0-4)   "slots": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#__codelineno-0-5)     "charm" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#__codelineno-0-6)   ], [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#__codelineno-0-7)   "icon": "accessories:gui/group/any" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#__codelineno-0-8) }`

| Field Keys | Data Type | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `"order"` | Integer | The order number to which the group will appear within the Accessories Screen with lower being placed first and higher numbers being placed last |
| `"slots"` | String\[\] | The slot names to which belong to the given Slot Group |
| `"icon"` | String | The resource location of the given slot icon in which is used to find the texture within the block atlas |

* * *

Last update: 2024-12-26

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/slot_groups/#)

---

# Adding support for Custom Packets - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#making-an-entrypoint)

Adding support for Custom Packets
=================================

While gadget has automatic support for almost all vanilla packets and some common mod packets, unknown custom payload packets are represented as their hex dumps, as gadget has no idea what that packet's structure is or how to display it. This page is meant to help you implement support for your packets so that you can easily view them in dumps.

Info

If you use a library to add your network packets, then your packets might be already fully supported. Packets using [oωo networking](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/owo/networking/)
 or [Fabric API packet-object networking](https://github.com/FabricMC/fabric/blob/1.20.1/fabric-networking-api-v1/src/main/java/net/fabricmc/fabric/api/networking/v1/FabricPacket.java#L22-L61)
 are automatically displayed as the actual packet object.

Making an entrypoint[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#making-an-entrypoint "Permanent link")

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

An easy way to run some code only when gadget is installed are the `gadget:init` and `gadget:client_init` entrypoints. They are run right after gadget main/client init, and any errors are logged and swallowed to avoid crashes.

fabric.mod.jsonExampleGadgetEntrypoint.java

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-0-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-0-2)     // ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-0-3)     "entrypoints": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-0-4)         "gadget:init": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-0-5)             "com.example.examplemod.ExampleGadgetEntrypoint" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-0-6)         ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-0-7)     }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-0-8)     // ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-0-9) }`

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-1-1) package com.example.examplemod; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-1-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-1-3) import io.wispforest.gadget.GadgetEntrypoint; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-1-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-1-5) public class ExampleGadgetEntrypoint implements GadgetEntrypoint { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-1-6)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-1-7)     public void onGadgetInit() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-1-8)         // Register all your stuff here... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-1-9)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-1-10) }`

`PacketUnwrapper.EVENT`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#packetunwrapperevent "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

While most of the functions of the dump viewer are served by separate events, the most convenient way to implement support for custom packets is the `PacketUnwrapper` event, as all other events have handlers that just try unwrap the packet and then call the needed methods on it, which centralizes everything you need to do with the packet into one class.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-2-1) PacketUnwrapper.EVENT.register((packet, errSink) -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-2-2)     if (!Objects.equals(packet.channelId(), BeepPacket.ID)) return null; // (1) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-2-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-2-4)     PacketByteBuf buf = NetworkUtil.unwrapCustom(packet.packet()); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-2-5) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-2-6)     return new UnwrappedBeepPacket(BeepPacket.read(buf)); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-2-7) });`

1.  You might also want to check whether `packet.state()` is the correct network state for your packet.

Additionally, gadget provides some nice utility interfaces that implement most of these methods for you, which can make the packet implementation even simpler.

### `FieldsUnwrappedPacket`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#fieldsunwrappedpacket "Permanent link")

This helper interface is mainly made for packets which are just wrappers around some arbitrary Java object, which should be shown as the values of all its fields. The only required method is `rawFieldsObject`, which should return the object that is supposed to be inspected.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-1) public record UnwrappedBeepPacket(BeepPacket packet) implements FieldsUnwrappedPacket { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-2)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-3)     public @Nullable Object rawFieldsObject() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-4)         return packet; // (1) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-5)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-7)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-8)     public Text headText() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-9)         return null; // (2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-10)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-3-11) }`

1.  If you don't have any other relevant data in the packet, you can just return `null` here to skip all field dumping.
2.  Any text returned here will be shown before the fields of the provided object. The default implementation returns the class of the object, so we just return `null` here to bypass that.

![examplemod:beep packet in the dump viewer](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/custom_packets_fields_example.png)

### `LinesUnwrappedPacket`[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#linesunwrappedpacket "Permanent link")

This is a more general helper interface meant for packets which can be easily rendered as rich `Text`. While this is incredibly convenient for simple packets, more complex packets should just implement `UnwrappedPacket` themselves.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-4-1) public record UnwrappedBeepPacket(BeepPacket packet) implements LinesUnwrappedPacket { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-4-2)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-4-3)     public void render(Consumer<Text> out, ErrorSink errSink) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-4-4)         out.accept(Text.literal("beepVolume") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-4-5)             .append(Text.literal(" = \"" + packet.beepVolume() + "\"") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-4-6)                 .formatted(Formatting.GRAY))); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-4-7)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-4-8) }`

![examplemod:beep packet in the dump viewer](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/gadget/custom_packets_lines_example.png)

Fully custom implementation[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#fully-custom-implementation "Permanent link")

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Although the unwrapped packet helper interfaces are convenient for a lot of cases, they sometimes don't cut it, especially for rather complex packets. Additionally, you might not even want to use the packet unwrapper event, as the separate events allow modifying other mods' packets without completely replacing them. The solution is to manually implement all event handlers/methods to fully customize how your packet looks.

Info

The `ErrorSink` objects given to most events are meant to be a sink for all non-fatal errors that an event handler can encounter. You don't have to use one if you don't want to catch your exceptions - all event handlers are try/catched and errors are reported.

### owo-ui rendering[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#owo-ui-rendering "Permanent link")

`UnwrappedPacket.render`  
`PacketRenderer.EVENT`

Arguably the most important feature a packet can have is an owo-ui renderer, as it determines how it will look in the dump viewer. The renderer has almost complete freedom as to how the packet is rendered, as you can insert any owo-ui component into the provided `out` flow layout.

UnwrappedPacket.renderPacketRenderer.EVENT

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-5-1) public record UnwrappedBeepPacket(BeepPacket packet) implements UnwrappedPacket { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-5-2)     @Environment(EnvType.CLIENT) // (1) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-5-3)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-5-4)     public void render(FlowLayout out, ErrorSink errSink) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-5-5)         out.child(Components.label(Text.literal("beep!"))); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-5-6)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-5-7) }`

1.  The `render` method should generally always be client-only to deter possible classloading issues if you reference a client-only class.

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-6-1) PacketRenderer.EVENT.register((packet, out, errSink) -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-6-2)     if (!Objects.equals(packet.channelId(), BeepPacket.ID)) return; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-6-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-6-4)     out.child(Components.label(Text.literal("beep!"))); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-6-5) });`

### Search text gathering[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#search-text-gathering "Permanent link")

`UnwrappedPacket.gatherSearchText`  
`SearchTextGatherer.EVENT`

The packet's search text determines whether it will be filtered by the search box - packets are only shown if all of the search words are included in the search text. The dump statistics screen also uses search text to group packets by type, so the search text should be kept clean and not have any extraneous data. That said, if you have some packet ID or other important packet type data, you should probably include it here.

UnwrappedPacket.gatherSearchTextSearchTextGatherer.EVENT

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-7-1) public record UnwrappedBeepPacket(BeepPacket packet) implements UnwrappedPacket { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-7-2)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-7-3)     public void gatherSearchText(StringBuilder out, ErrorSink errSink) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-7-4)         out.append(" ").append(packet.beepVolume()); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-7-5)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-7-6) }`

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-8-1) SearchTextGatherer.EVENT.register((packet, out, errSink) -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-8-2)     if (!Objects.equals(packet.channelId(), BeepPacket.ID)) return; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-8-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-8-4)     PacketByteBuf buf = NetworkUtil.unwrapCustom(packet.packet()); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-8-5)     BeepPacket beep = BeepPacket.read(buf); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-8-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-8-7)     out.append(" ").append(beep.beepVolume()); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-8-8) });`

### Plain text dumping[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#plain-text-dumping "Permanent link")

`UnwrappedPacket.dumpAsPlainText`  
`PlainTextPacketDumper.EVENT`

This handler is used whenever the user exports the packet dump as plain text. While the format of what you dump is ultimately up to you, the plain text dump uses indentation to represent trees of data and uses mostly ASCII characters.

UnwrappedPacket.dumpAsPlainTextPlainTextPacketDumper.EVENT

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-9-1) public record UnwrappedBeepPacket(BeepPacket packet) implements UnwrappedPacket { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-9-2)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-9-3)     public void dumpAsPlainText(FormattedDumper out, int indent, ErrorSink errSink) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-9-4)         out.write(indent, "beep packet!"); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-9-5)         out.write(indent + 1, "volume = " + packet.beepVolume()); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-9-6)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-9-7) }`

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-10-1) PlainTextPacketDumper.EVENT.register((packet, out, indent, errSink) -> { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-10-2)     if (!Objects.equals(packet.channelId(), BeepPacket.ID)) return; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-10-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-10-4)     PacketByteBuf buf = NetworkUtil.unwrapCustom(packet.packet()); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-10-5)     BeepPacket beep = BeepPacket.read(buf); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-10-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-10-7)     out.write(indent, "beep packet!"); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-10-8)     out.write(indent + 1, "volume = " + beep.beepVolume()); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/gadget/packet-dumps/custom_packets/#__codelineno-10-9) });`

# Adjusting Slot Amount - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#slot-adjustments-methods)

Slot Adjustments Methods[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#slot-adjustments-methods "Permanent link")

====================================================================================================================================================

Slots were designed with the potential for the given slot amount to be changeable. This can be accomplished either by using the data format through the various `operation` type's, or by using the other methods provided.

Attribute Modifier[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#attribute-modifier "Permanent link")

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Accessories adds a system for adjusting a specific Slot types amount of slots given to the entity who equips the Accessory. Such can be done either though a programmatic or the Data Component way.

### Programmatic Method[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#programmatic-method "Permanent link")

Accessories provides a programmatic way of adjusting slot amounts, which is similar in design to the data pack method. The method calls for this are found either on the `AccessoriesCapability` or the targeted `AccessoriesContainer` itself.

The following example shows how to add and remove additional ring slots, using the capability within a test Accessory:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-1) public class RingIncreaser implements Accessory { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-2)     private static final ResourceLocation RING_ATTRIBUTE_LOCATION = ResourceLocation.fromNamespaceAndPath("test", "additional_rings") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-4)     //... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-5)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-6)     public void onEquip(ItemStack stack, SlotReference reference) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-7)         var map = HashMultimap.<String, AttributeModifier>create(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-8) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-9)         map.put("ring", new AttributeModifier(RING_ATTRIBUTE_LOCATION, 100, AttributeModifier.Operation.ADDITION)); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-10) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-11)         reference.capability().addTransientSlotModifiers(map); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-12)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-13) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-14)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-15)     public void onUnequip(ItemStack stack, SlotReference reference) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-16)         var map = HashMultimap.<String, AttributeModifier>create(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-17) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-18)         map.put("ring", new AttributeModifier(RING_ATTRIBUTE_LOCATION, 100, AttributeModifier.Operation.ADDITION)); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-19) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-20)         reference.capability().removeSlotModifiers(map); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-21)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-22)     //... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-0-23) }`

Another Programmatic method of such is by adjusting the slots Dynamic Modifiers instead of adding to entity on equipping of the accessory:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-1) public class HatIncreaser implements Accessory { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-2)     private static final ResourceLocation HAT_ATTRIBUTE_LOCATION = ResourceLocation.fromNamespaceAndPath("test", "additional_hats") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-4)     //... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-5)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-6)     public void getDynamicModifiers(ItemStack stack, SlotReference reference, AccessoryAttributeBuilder builder){ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-7)         // Exclusive Refers to only one instance of the modifier is allowed  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-8)         builder.addExclusive(SlotAttribute.getSlotAttribute("hat"), HAT_ATTRIBUTE_LOCATION, 4, AttributeModifier.Operation.ADDITION); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-9) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-10)         // Stackable Refers to any amount of the given modifier is allowed (Preappends Slot Info like the type and index to the location) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-11)         builder.addStackable(SlotAttribute.getSlotAttribute("hat"), HAT_ATTRIBUTE_LOCATION, 4, AttributeModifier.Operation.ADDITION); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-12)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-13)     //... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-1-14) }`

### Data Component[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#data-component "Permanent link")

As outlined within the [`accessories:attributes`](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/itemstack_components/#attribute-modifiers)
 Item Component you can add such to a given ItemStack to adjust the amount of equippable slots _when the accessory is equipped_.

Config File[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#config-file "Permanent link")

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Accessories config file allows you to adjust the slot amount globally. Keep in mind that changing the defaults can heavily change the balance of your game/modpack. You can go well above a hundred ring slots for example, although that would easily clutter up your Accessory screen.

The config file is located within the `./config/` folder within your Minecraft instance under the file `accessories`. You can then specify new slot amounts using the `"modifiers`" field in the given format:

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-2-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-2-2)     //... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-2-3)     "modifiers": [ // Array of json objects comprising the below structure [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-2-4)         { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-2-5)             "slotType": "test", // Targeted Slot Name [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-2-6)             "amount": 23 // The Amount to shoot for as the base [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-2-7)         } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-2-8)     ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#__codelineno-2-9) }`

* * *

Last update: 2024-12-26

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/general/adjusting_slot_amount/#)

# Rendering API Breakdown - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/rendering_api/#transformation-methods)

Rendering API Breakdown
=======================

To link a given item to a specific `AccessoryRenderer` you will need to register such within the `AccessoriesRendererRegistry` class. By **default** all accessory items that have no renderer registered will get the `DefaultAccessoryRenderer` which attempts to render the block/item on the player in a position where the slot is located on the entity.

Default Accessory Rendering Behavior

All default slots have default renderers, but new slots will need to implement these on their own using the `DefaultAccessoryRenderer#registerHelper` method. Such helper is just a generic helper to transform the renderer to the slots location on the entity.

The only way for one to disable the Default Rendering for a given Accessory is by using the `AccessoriesRendererRegistry#registerNoRenderer` or adjusting the Data Component if actively toggled on. Furthermore the given default Render can be manipulated using the [`AccessoryRenderTransformations` data component](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/itemstack_components/#transformations)
 for use with Data driven Accessories.

If you need simple item rendering for your Accessory, then you could look at [`SimpleAccessoryRenderer`](https://github.com/wisp-forest/accessories/blob/1.21.4/common/src/main/java/io/wispforest/accessories/api/client/SimpleAccessoryRenderer.java)
. It provides a `align` method, which lets you transform the rendering to your desired location on the entity.

Transformation Methods[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/rendering_api/#transformation-methods "Permanent link")

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Accessories provides some helper methods to assist with transforming your `AccessoryRenderer` to various locations on the body with the primary method being `transformToModelPart` which will transform the given `PoseStack` (`MatrixStack`) to a given location on the targeted `ModelPart`.

Two overloads exist for this. The first method transforms the `PoseStack` (`MatrixStack`) to the center of the `ModelPart` while the other allows for more control on the positioning on the `x`, `y`, and `z` axis by providing a number between `-1` and `1` as explained below:

| Axis | Negative Values | Positive Values |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `x` | Left Movement | Right Movement |
| `y` | Bottom Movement | Top Movement |
| `z` | Back Movement | Front Movement |

This method of transformation allows for the Accessories renderer to follow the model parts better allowing for compatibility with mods like Entity Model Feature and is more precises than generic transformations to where given model part may be located.

Furthermore you can use `transformToFace` to target specific faces of a given model part by passing the given `Side` which such will transform the rendering to the outside of the given models face.

First Person Rendering

Accessories supports rendering within first person. By default anything on the humanoid entities arms is rendered this way. You can set this yourself by overriding the [`shouldRenderInFirstPerson`](https://github.com/wisp-forest/accessories/blob/fa06f044f5c7486b26a8c0774f7ca3edbd256cad/common/src/main/java/io/wispforest/accessories/api/client/AccessoryRenderer.java#L76)
 method within your renderer.

* * *

Last update: 2024-12-26

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/rendering_api/#)

# Setup Environment - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#multiloader)

Setup Environment
=================

Accessories supports both **Fabric** and **Neoforge**, and also support mods that are multiplatform by offering a **Common** target.

GroovyKotlin

To start you will need to add the following mavens to your `build.gradle`:

build.gradle

    `[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-0-1)     maven { url 'https://maven.wispforest.io/releases' } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-0-2)     maven { url 'https://maven.su5ed.dev/releases' } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-0-3)     maven { url 'https://maven.fabricmc.net' }`

After declaring such, you will need to add the dependency within the `dependencies` block while also specifying the `accessories_version` within your `gradle.properties`:

FabricNeoforge

build.gradle

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-1-1) dependencies { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-1-2)     modImplementation("io.wispforest:accessories-fabric:${project.accessories_version}") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-1-3) }`

build.gradle

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-2-1) dependencies { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-2-2)     implementation("io.wispforest:accessories-neoforge:${project.accessories_version}") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-2-3) }`

#### Multiloader[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#multiloader "Permanent link")

Common - ArchNeoforge - ArchCommon - Vanilla Gradle

build.gradle

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-3-1) dependencies { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-3-2)     modImplementation("io.wispforest:accessories-common:${project.accessories_version}") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-3-3) }`

build.gradle

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-4-1) dependencies { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-4-2)     modImplementation("io.wispforest:accessories-neoforge:${project.accessories_version}") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-4-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-4-4)     // Required due to issues with JIJ dependency resolving in arch or something [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-4-5)     forgeRuntimeLibrary("blue.endless:jankson:1.2.2") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-4-6)     forgeRuntimeLibrary("io.wispforest:endec:0.1.9") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-4-7)     forgeRuntimeLibrary("io.wispforest.endec:gson:0.1.5") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-4-8)     forgeRuntimeLibrary("io.wispforest.endec:jankson:0.1.6") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-4-9)     forgeRuntimeLibrary("io.wispforest.endec:netty:0.1.6") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-4-10) }`

build.gradle

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-5-1) dependencies { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-5-2)     // Yarn Intermediary  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-5-3)     compileOnly("io.wispforest:accessories-common:${project.accessories_version}") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-5-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-5-5)     // Mojang Mappings [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-5-6)     compileOnly("io.wispforest:accessories-common:${project.accessories_version}-mojmap") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-5-7) }`

To start you will need to add the following mavens to your `build.gradle`:

build.gradle.kts

    `[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-6-1)     maven("https://maven.wispforest.io/releases") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-6-2)     maven("https://maven.su5ed.dev/releases") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-6-3)     maven("https://maven.fabricmc.net")`

Common - ArchNeoforge - ArchCommon - Vanilla Gradle

build.gradle.kts

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-11-1) dependencies { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-11-2)     // Yarn Intermediary  [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-11-3)     compileOnly("io.wispforest:accessories-common:${properties["accessories_version"]}") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-11-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-11-5)     // Mojang Mappings [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-11-6)     compileOnly("io.wispforest:accessories-common:${properties["accessories_version"]}-mojmap") [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/dev_setup/#__codelineno-11-7) }`

Tip

It is recommended to get the latest version either from Modrinth, Curseforge or check the [Maven](https://maven.wispforest.io/#/releases/io/wispforest/accessories-common)
 for latest dev builds.

# API Fundamentals - Wisp Forest Docs

 

[Skip to content](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/api_fundamentals/#creating-an-accessory)

API Fundamentals
================

### Creating an Accessory[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/api_fundamentals/#creating-an-accessory "Permanent link")

You can either create an Accessory by implementing the `Accessory` interface or by extending the `AccessoryItem` which implements the `Accessory` interface.

The first requires that you register your custom `Accessory` to the given `Item` using the `AccessoryRegistry#register` method. Using the `AccessoryItem` class will automatically register the accessory when the class is instantiated.

This `Accessory` interface contains various functions that can be performed. Some examples include `tick`ing, controlling equipability, listening to when equipment is changed, adding attribute modifiers (dynamically or statically), and adding custom tooltip info.

### Adding a Custom Accessory Renderer[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/api_fundamentals/#adding-a-custom-accessory-renderer "Permanent link")

Creating a custom `Accessory` comes with the ability to add some rendering that is attached to the player. You can do so by creating a custom instance of `AccessoryRenderer` and registering it using the `AccessoriesRendererRegistry.registerRenderer` method. More information about the rendering API be found in the [rendering API section](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/rendering_api/)
.

Default Rendering Behavior

By default within the Rendering API: all Accessories will use `DefaultAccessoryRenderer`, unless a custom `AccessoryRenderer` is registered, or an explicit "no renderer" is registered using `AccessoriesRendererRegistry#registerNoRenderer`.

### Creating a custom Slot Predicate[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/api_fundamentals/#creating-a-custom-slot-predicate "Permanent link")

In cases where neither a Tag or using Data Components on your Item Stack are suitable, you may create a custom `SlotBasedPredicate` where you can have more control over what `Accessory` entries are allowed to be equipped in a given slot.

This is useful for dynamic accessory types that may have multiple iterations that would make it difficult to use a Item Tag without possible issues.

Entity Based Predicate

With the release of 1.2.0, `EntityBasedPredicate` exists as a way to have entity context when evaluating if a given Accessory should be equipped within a given slot. It is recommend that this is used only if needed, as it can be difficult to evaluate for cases like crafting where the target entity may differ.

### Accessing The Capability[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/api_fundamentals/#accessing-the-capability "Permanent link")

Within Accessories there is the `AccessoriesCapability` which is used to access the slot containers, adjust slot attributes, or query the inventory for various possible item stacks.

Any interaction involving a given entity will be exposed in its `AccessoriesCapability`, which only exists if the entity has slots bound it. Make sure to write your logic to respect the fact that not every entity has slots bound to it (since the capability could be `null`).

### Adjusting Accessory Equipping[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/api_fundamentals/#adjusting-accessory-equipping "Permanent link")

A considerable difference between other Accessory API's is that `canEquip` is checked when Accessory data is loaded, and revalidated on reload. This requires you to use `isAnotherEquipped` found on the given entities `AccessoriesCapability` to prevent duplicate Accessory items from being equipped. This requires the current `ItemStack` and its `SlotReference` to be ignored when checking for another equipped accessory.

### Dealing with the Container[¶](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/api_fundamentals/#dealing-with-the-container "Permanent link")

For each slot on an entity - there will be an `AccessoriesContainer` instance if the given Entity has the slot bound to it. Bear in mind that when checking this, the slot you specify may not exist on the entity (it can be `null`).

This object allows for getting information like the current equipped accessories, render toggles for given accessories and managing the slot attributes stored. It mainly not recommend to directly use the container to look for Accessories but instead use the methods on `AccessoriesCapability` instead.

* * *

Last update: 2024-12-25

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/accessories/developer/api_fundamentals/#)

# Setup - Wisp Forest Docs

 

Setup
=====

To start setting up your addon, add an optional dependency on Limelight:

gradle.propertiesbuild.gradle

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-0-1) limelight_version=...`

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-1-1) repositories { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-1-2)     maven { url 'https://maven.wispforest.io/releases/' } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-1-3) } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-1-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-1-5) dependencies { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-1-6)     modCompileOnly "io.wispforest:limelight:${project.limelight_version}" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-1-7)     modLocalRuntime "io.wispforest:limelight:${project.limelight_version}" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-1-8) }`

Now that you have Limelight's code in your development environment, you need to define a Limelight entrypoint:

fabric.mod.jsonExampleLimelightCompat.java

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-2)     // ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-3) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-4)     "entrypoints": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-5)         "limelight": [ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-6)             "com.example.exampleextension.ExampleLimelightCompat" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-7)         ] [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-8)     }, [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-9) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-10)     // ... [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-2-11) }`

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-1) package com.example.exampleextension; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-2) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-3) import io.wispforest.limelight.api.LimelightEntrypoint; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-4) import io.wispforest.limelight.api.extension.LimelightExtension; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-5) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-6) import java.util.function.Consumer; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-8) public class ExampleLimelightCompat implements LimelightEntrypoint { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-9)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-10)     public void registerExtensions(Consumer<LimelightExtension> extensionRegistry) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-11)         // Register extensions here! [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-12)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/setup/#__codelineno-3-13) }`

Continue by [adding an extension](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/)
.

* * *

Last update: 2024-09-04

# Defining Extensions - Wisp Forest Docs

 

Defining Extensions
===================

A `LimelightExtension` is the basic building block of extending Limelight functionality. Limelight has several built-in extensions, but if you're adding Limelight compatibility or making a Limelight addon mod, you probably want to make your own extension.

Extensions can be individually disabled by the user, so if your addon is adding many unrelated sets of functionality, it is advised to make them separate extensions.

You can define and register an extension like so:

MyFunExtension.javaExampleLimelightCompat.java

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-0-1) public class MyFunExtension implements LimelightExtension { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-0-2)     public static final Identifier ID = Identifier.of("example-extension", "my_fun_extension"); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-0-3)     public static final MyFunExtension INSTANCE = new MyFunExtension(); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-0-4) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-0-5)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-0-6)     public Identifier id() { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-0-7)         return ID; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-0-8)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-0-9) }`

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-1-1) public class ExampleLimelightCompat implements LimelightEntrypoint { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-1-2)     @Override [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-1-3)     public void registerExtensions(Consumer<LimelightExtension> extensionRegistry) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-1-4)         extensionRegistry.accept(MyFunExtension.INSTANCE); [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-1-5)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-1-6) }`

You also need[1](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#fn:1)
 to provide a translatable title for the extension (and optionally a description):

en\_us.json

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-2-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-2-2)     "limelightExtension.example-extension.my_fun_extension": "My Fun Extension", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-2-3)     "limelightExtension.example-extension.my_fun_extension.desc": "Does very fun stuff!" [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#__codelineno-2-4) }`

This results in this Limelight config screen entry: ![a config entry for My Fun Extension](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/assets/limelight/my_fun_extension_entry.png)

* * *

1.  You can also override the `LimelightExtension#name` and `LimelightExtension#description` methods. [↩](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#fnref:1 "Jump back to footnote 1 in the text")
    

* * *

Last update: 2024-08-30

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/defining_extensions/#)

# Adding Wikis - Wisp Forest Docs

 

Adding Wikis
============

The **Wiki** (`limelight:wiki`) extension has built-in support for querying the [Minecraft Wiki](https://minecraft.wiki/)
, but you might want to add support for other wikis (e.g. your mod's wiki). For this use case, Limelight has a resource-pack-based way to add custom wikis (which is used for the default Minecraft Wiki!).

Wikis are defined as resources under `assets/<namespace>/limelight/wiki/<wikiname>.json`, and have this schema:

``[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-1) interface WikiDescription { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-2)     /** [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-3)      * The title of this wiki, to be shown in the results. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-4)      * This uses the vanilla JSON text format. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-5)      */ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-6)     title: JSONTextComponent; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-7) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-8)     /** [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-9)      * A key that can be used to quickly search in this wiki via a bang. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-10)      * For example, `mcwiki` allows you to search like `!mcwiki Creeper` [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-11)      */ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-12)     bangKey?: string; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-13) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-14)     /** [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-15)      * The type of this wiki. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-16)      * Limelight supports MediaWiki and MkDocs wikis by default, but new wiki sources [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-17)      * can be added by Limelight addons. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-18)      */ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-19)     type: "limelight:media_wiki" | "limelight:mkdocs" | string; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-20) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-21)     /** [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-22)      * The source of this wiki. Specific to this wiki's `type`. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-23)      */ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-24)     source: unknown; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-25) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-26)     /** [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-27)      * Language-specific source overrides. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-28)      * Keys are language identifiers used by Minecraft and values are wiki sources. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-29)      */ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-30)     languageOverrides?: { [languageKey: string]: unknown }; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-0-31) };``

For example, here's a wiki definition for the docs site you're currently on:

assets/example-pack/limelight/wiki/wisp\_forest.json

`[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-1-1) { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-1-2)     "type": "limelight:mkdocs", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-1-3)     "title": "Wisp Forest", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-1-4)     "bang_key": "wispforest", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-1-5)     "source": { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-1-6)         "url": "https://docs.wispforest.io", [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-1-7)         "includeParagraphs": false [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-1-8)     } [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-1-9) }`

There are two built-in wiki source types in Limelight, though [you can always add your own](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/extending/adding_wiki_sources/)
:

*   MediaWiki (`limelight:media_wiki`)  
    The wiki software used by Wikipedia and the Minecraft Wiki.
    
    `[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-2-1) interface MediaWikiSource { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-2-2)     /** [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-2-3)      * The MediaWiki API for this wiki. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-2-4)      * For example, the English Minecraft Wiki's API is located at https://minecraft.wiki/api.php [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-2-5)      */ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-2-6)     url: string; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-2-7) }`
    
*   MkDocs (`limelight:mkdocs`)  
    The static site generator used by the Wisp Forest Docs.
    
    ``[](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-1) interface MkDocsWikiSource { [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-2)     /** [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-3)      * The base URL of this wiki. (e.g. https://docs.wispforest.io for these docs) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-4)     */ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-5)     url: string; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-6) [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-7)     /** [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-8)      * Whether to include specific paragraphs of pages in the results. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-9)     * Defaults to `false`. [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-10)     */ [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-11)     includeParagraphs?: boolean; [](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#__codelineno-3-12) }``
    

* * *

Last update: 2024-08-30

[Back to top](https://docs.wispforest.io/legacy/limelight/configuring/adding_wikis/#)
